601 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schiefelbein


No. M2005-00166-CCA-R3-CD and No. M2005-02370-CCA-R10-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


230 S.W.3d 88; 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 138


February 14, 2006, Session  
February 8, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Remanded by State v. Schiefelbein, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 214 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 7, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Schiefelbein v. Morrow, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 100396 (M.D. Tenn., July 16, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 & 10; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed in Part as Modified; Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. I-1102-427. Russ Heldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed in Part as Modified; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, jury convicted defendant of 7 counts of aggravated sexual battery, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-504(a)(4), and 1 count of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1005. He was sentenced to 96 years in prison. He filed a direct appeal and also pursued interlocutory review to bar future prosecution of 3 severed child-rape charges, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-522 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Although the trial errors cited by defendant did not require reversal of his convictions, his 96-year sentence (eight 12-year consecutive sentences), while permissible under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(5) (2003), was not reasonably related to the severity of his offenses. The circumstances of the case required modification of his effective sentence from 96 years to 36 years. The judge who presided at defendant's trial was disqualified from conducting further proceedings in the case because of his punitive reaction toward trial counsel's comments about trial error, his failure to place on the record his findings and reasons for denying defendant's motion to recuse, his restrictions of defendant's right of discovery, and his credibility-bolstering of the victim-witness. The child-rape offenses were improperly severed under the criteria of Tenn. R. Crim. P. 8(a)(1)(A) and 14(b)(2)(A), and were barred from future prosecution by the principles of double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 10, because the rape charges were included within the broad time frame alleged in the indictment and the time frame specified in the bill of particulars.


OUTCOME: Defendant's effective sentence was modified to 36 years, but defendant's convictions and sentences were otherwise affirmed. The State was barred from proceeding further on the three counts of child rape, and those charges were dismissed. The judge who presided at trial was disqualified from conducting further proceedings in the case.

 

602 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Williamson v. State


No. W2006-00576-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 87



February 1, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Williamson v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 609 (Tenn., June 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Tipton County. No. 3536. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.
State v. Williamson, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 337 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 27, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Tipton County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief. The State of Tennessee filed a motion requesting that the court affirm the denial of postconviction relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of especially aggravated robbery. The trial court sentenced him to 22 years in prison. His conviction and sentence were upheld on direct appeal. The trial court denied petitioner postconviction relief on the ground that his petition was untimely. On appeal, petitioner argued that he was entitled to postconviction relief based on newly discovered evidence in the alleged form of a photographic lineup when his mother discovered the same in his criminal records filed at the county clerk's office. The court found that the photographic lineup could not be construed as scientific evidence. The court could not conclude that the particular factual circumstances tolled the limitations period. The postconviction petition was not filed until well beyond the one-year statute of limitations in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a). The grounds for relief alleged by petitioner did not fall within any of the exceptions to the statute of limitations in § 40-30-102(b).


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

603 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Skipper


No. E2006-00785-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 53


November 14, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
January 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 26, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Loudon County. No. 10742 E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Loudon County (Tennessee) of assault, resisting arrest, and obstruction of the execution of an arrest warrant. After her motion for a new trial was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury that officers could only enter a residence with both an arrest warrant and a reasonable belief that the person they were seeking was located therein. Second, defendant claimed that the trial court erred by not instructing the jury on defendant's affirmative defense of use of force in her home when the defendant reasonably believed that law enforcement officers were unlawfully entering her home without a search warrant, exigent circumstances, or an arrest warrant coupled with the reasonable belief that the person they sought was in her home. The court of appeals disagreed. The State responded that the trial court did not err because the jury was properly instructed on self-defense and no further special instructions were submitted to the trial court in writing. Because Tenn. R. Crim. P. 30 envisioned that requests be made in writing, oral requests for instructions were not sufficient for the court of appeals to find that the trial court's instructions were improper. Therefore, the trial court did not err by denying defendant's oral proposal of jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

604 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dobbins


No. M2005-01987-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


265 S.W.3d 419; 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 9


September 19, 2006, Session  
January 5, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2004-B-1499. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which convicted him of driving under the influence (DUI), in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401(a)(1) (2004).


OVERVIEW: An officer, while on routine patrol about 2:00 a.m., drove into the parking lot of a public park. The parking lot was not gated and had only one access road. The officer noticed a car parked at the far end of the parking lot. As the officer drove toward the car, its headlights came on, and it started to drive off toward the entrance of the park. The officer activated his blue lights, stopped the car, and discovered defendant in the driver's seat. Defendant was subsequently arrested and convicted of DUI. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the parking lot was a premises generally frequented by the public at large. Even if after-hours patrons of the park went there to conduct illegal activity and even though the going itself was a misdemeanor, there was nothing in the proscription of DUI that required that those who frequented a property had to be somehow cross-representative of the general public. Further, when defendant saw the approach of the police cruiser and began to drive toward the parking lot's exit in an impaired state, he attempted to commit DUI pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-12-101(a)(3) (2003).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Stevens v. State


No. M2005-00096-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1020


July 18, 2006, Session  
December 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Stevens v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 511 (Tenn., May 21, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stevens v. Tennessee, 552 U.S. 1064, 128 S. Ct. 708, 169 L. Ed. 2d 557, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12898 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 98-A-625. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.
State v. Stevens, 78 S.W.3d 817, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 223 (Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree premeditated murder and one count of especially aggravated robbery and was sentenced to death. The Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) denied his petition for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for hiring his neighbor to kill his wife and his mother-in-law. On appeal, the court held that the postconviction court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's request for a continuance of an evidentiary hearing, based on the resignation of one of the attorneys assigned to his case, because the attorney resigned three months before the hearing, and the remaining attorney offered no reasonable explanation why three months was an insufficient amount of time to review any work performed by the resigning attorney, especially given the fact that the remaining attorney had already been involved in the case for over a year. Defendant failed to show that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to exercise a peremptory challenge or challenge for cause a particular juror, after the juror wrote a letter to the judge and asked to be released based due to the fact that his practice would suffer in his absence and that he was pro-prosecution and pro-death penalty because at no time during the judge's questioning of the juror did he mention his view of capital punishment and defendant stated he had no objection to the juror.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

606 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


McGowan v. Bell


No. M2006-00149-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1016


November 29, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
December 21, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McGowan v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 284 (Tenn., Mar. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 00C-3729. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
McGowan v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 319 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 7, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant challenged the orders of the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissing his amended petition for writ of habeas corpus and his petition for writ of error coram nobis.


OVERVIEW: Upon the claim in the original petition for writ of habeas corpus that the applicant committed his second set of offenses while on bond from the first, the appellate court remanded the matter for the trial court to determine whether this was true and whether concurrent sentencing had been a condition of his plea agreement. However, the applicant withdrew these claims and sought to proceed on his claims raised in the amended petition. Thus, following the remand, the applicant abandoned the issue which the appellate court had directed be resolved and instead, embarked with an entirely new claim. The appellate court found that the applicant's withdrawing of the claims which were to be reviewed following the remand resulted in the habeas corpus court having nothing to review. The new claims, set out in the amended petition, were outside the remand instructions from the appellate court and thus, not properly before the habeas corpus court. Also, the habeas corpus court properly dismissed the petition for writ of error coram nobis, because the applicant sought to present evidence which was not "newly discovered."


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

607 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. Watson


No. M2005-02061-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1004


April 18, 2006, Session  
December 14, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. 1-CR-08554-04-2205-III. Russ Heldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner filed an application for habeas corpus relief in the Williamson County Circuit Court, Tennessee, to challenge his conviction for sixth offense driving on a revoked license. Relief was denied, and the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was sentenced to 11 months, 29 days, with all but 65 days suspended on supervised probation. The appellate court found that the petitioner's motion to alter or amend did not toll the commencement of the thirty-day period in which to file a notice of appeal. However, in the interest of justice, the appellate court waived the untimely notice and reviewed the petitioner's issues on the merits. The appellate court found that the petitioner had not proven that he was presently confined or restrained of his liberty under a void judgment or an expired sentence. The Tennessee habeas corpus statutes were clear that the petitioner seeking habeas relief must be in either actual or constructive custody of the sentence being challenged because the term "restrained of liberty" required either actual or constructive custody. The petitioner's sentence had expired prior to his appeal, and quite simply, habeas relief was not proper to the petitioner. Also, it was settled that the petitioner could waive his right to presentment, indictment, or impeachment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

608 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Austin v. State


No. W2005-02591-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 970


July 12, 2006, Session  
December 13, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. B58357-A. C. Creed McGinley, Judge.
State v. Austin, 87 S.W.3d 447, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 400 (Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for coram nobis without holding an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to death by a jury on March 5, 1999. In October 2004, his counsel filed a petition for writ of error coram nobis on the basis of newly discovered evidence pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-26-105 in the form of recanted testimony. Without holding an evidentiary hearing, the coram nobis court dismissed the petition, and the petitioner currently brought an appeal challenging the action. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, stating that the petition was properly denied without an evidentiary hearing because the first and third prong of the Mixon factors for determining the viability of a coram nobis petition had not been met. The inmate did not bolster his petition with any sworn statement of the witness who allegedly stated that he lied; the inmate merely alleged via a sworn statement from third parties that the witness had disclaimed his sworn resentencing hearing testimony. Moreover, the record was devoid of any claim of corroboration that the witness's recantation was truthful and that his resentencing hearing testimony was false. Additionally, different testimony by the witness would not have affected the imposition of the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

609 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammonds


No. M2005-01352-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 919


July 26, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
November 29, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sumner County. No. 347-2003. Jane Wheatcraft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Sumner County (Tennessee), which convicted him, after he pled guilty, to possession of over 26 grams of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pled guilty to possession of over 26 grams of cocaine and, pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37, he reserved four certified questions of law relating to whether the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress because the traffic stop and subsequent search were unconstitutional. Finding no error, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The appellate court stated that although it was clear that defendant was "seized" within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7, the questioning of defendant and the inquiry into his driver's license documentation did not exceed proper perimeters and create an unreasonable detention. Given the evidence elicited during the investigation, defendant's demeanor, and his lack of candor about being on probation for prior drug offenses, he was not unreasonably detained. Additionally, the officer had reasonable suspicion to conduct the search. Defendant was driving in the highest crime area in the county, he was nervous, and he was a known drug dealer and user who was on probation for drug offenses at the time of the stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Williams v. State


No. E2006-00230-CCA-R3-PC.


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 909


September 26, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
November 27, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. C51,608. Phyllis H. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee) to reckless aggravated assault and driving under the influence. After his request for postconviction and habeas corpus relief were denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals found, inter alia, that because petitioner did not allege that his convictions were void, or that his sentences had expired, the post-conviction court properly dismissed his petition for writ of habeas corpus. Moreover, the petition could have also been dismissed for failure to comply with the statutory mandate regarding venue for habeas corpus actions. Petitioner was incarcerated in Lake County but filed his habeas petition in the Criminal Court for Sullivan County, and his petition stated no reason why he did not file in Lake County. As such, petitioner failed to comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-105, and his petition was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

611 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Van Tran v. State


No. W2005-01334-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 899


May 2, 2006, Session  
November 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Tran v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 428 (Tenn., Apr. 16, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Van Tran v. Tenn., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12047 (U.S., Nov. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-14409. John P. Colton, Jr., Judge.
Van Tran v. State, 66 S.W.3d 790, 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 820 (Tenn., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denying his motion to reopen his postconviction petition for the limited purpose of determining whether he was mentally retarded under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203 and thus ineligible for the death penalty under the Eighth Amendment and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of three counts of felony murder and sentenced to death for his role in the killing of three victims during a restaurant robbery. The inmate sought postconviction relief arguing that he could not be put to death because he was mentally retarded. On appeal of the trial court's order, the court held that the inmate failed to prove that he was mentally retarded under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203 and therefore he was properly denied relief. The inmate failed to prove that he had deficits in adaptive behavior as the trial court correctly determined that little weight should be given to the inmate's below average score on the independent living scale, as the inmate had been diagnosed with paranoid schizophrenia and there was no indication that the testing questions took into account his lifestyle in Vietnam, his difficulty communicating in English, or the fact that he spent the majority of his adult life in jail. The circumstances of the crime also belied any assertion that the inmate suffered from any deficit in intellectual ability or adaptive skills. The inmate also failed to prove that mental retardation manifested during the developmental period.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate's motion to reopen his postconviction petition was affirmed.

Rucker v. State


No. E2005-01713-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 874



November 8, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Morgan County. No. 8992. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.
State v. Rucker, 712 S.W.2d 482, 1986 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 2589 (Tenn. Crim. App., 1986)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Morgan County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition for writ of habeas corpus. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of assault with intent to commit murder in the first degree with bodily injury, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, and assault with intent to commit murder in the first degree. He received a life sentence, forty years, and twenty years, respectively. The petitioner filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus; however, the petition failed to establish a cognizable claim for relief. Petitioner's sentence of life plus sixty years had not expired, and his petition did not show a void judgment. His motion for DNA analysis remained pending in the trial court and was not ripe for appellate review. Petitioner's claim of a defective indictment based on the failure to include the statutory aggravating factors potentially applicable in capital murder sentencing proceedings did not entitle him to relief. His Apprendi argument raised for the first time on appeal was not subject to review.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Fitch


No. W2004-02833-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 862


May 2, 2006, Session  
November 2, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Fitch, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 203 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Fitch v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 199 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded for Re-sentencing. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 02-07320. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded for Re-sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Criminal Court (Tennessee), which convicted defendant, after a jury trial of first-degree premeditated murder, and which sentenced defendant, after a separate penalty phase, to death. The jury had found the presence of two statutory aggravating circumstances and had found that the aggravating factors outweighed any mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering the victim, his estranged girlfriend. The court agreed with the trial court that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated when the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant was advised of his Miranda rights and, although intoxicated, was sufficiently aware of his surroundings to understand and consent to a waiver of those rights. Evidence was sufficient for the jury to infer that defendant's conduct was premeditated, as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1). The evidence showed, in part, that defendant ambushed the victim at work, secured a weapon prior to the murder and later concealed the weapon, and fired numerous rounds at the victim. It was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to admit pictures of the crime scene and of the autopsy. When considering whether defendant's prior conviction for reckless endangerment qualified as a prior violent felony for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2), it was error for the trial court to consider the affidavit of complaint pertaining to the prior conviction. The court could not conclude that the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for first degree murder. The court reversed the imposition of the death sentence and remanded the matter for a new sentencing hearing.

 

614 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Atwood v. State


No. M2006-01678-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 848



November 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Atwood v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 62 (Tenn., Jan. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dickson County. No. CR-5524. Robert E. Burch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dickson County (Tennessee) convicted petitioner inmate of burglary. The trial court summarily dismissed the inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief. The inmate appealed the trial court's summary dismissal of his petition. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court's denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's habeas petition alleged that his guilty plea was not knowingly and voluntarily entered because he received the ineffective assistance of counsel. He also alleged that his sentence was unconstitutionally imposed. The inmate first alleged that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel which rendered his guilty plea involuntary and unknowing. Those allegations, if true, would render the convictions and sentences voidable, but not void. If the allegations in a petition for habeas corpus relief did not demonstrate that the judgment was void, the trial court could correctly dismiss the petition without a hearing. In addition, the Tennessee Supreme Court determined that the Blakely decision did not announce a new rule of law and that Tennessee's sentencing structure, under which the inmate was sentenced, did not violate the inmate's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial. Finally, the appellate court had previously held that Blakely did not apply retroactively to cases on collateral appeal. Thus, the trial court did not err by summarily dismissing the inmate's habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

615 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wallace


No. W2005-01927-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 858


May 2, 2006, Session  
November 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Wallace, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 339 (Tenn., Mar. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardin County. No. 8392. C. Creed McGinley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardin County (Tennessee), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of possession of cocaine over point five (0.5) grams with intent to sell, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417(c)(1), and possession of marijuana, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-418(a) (2003). Defendant was sentenced to twenty-five years and eleven months and twenty-nine days imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A woman claimed that she was a guest at the hotel and consented to the officers' search of the room in which several people, including defendant, were located. Officers found drug paraphernalia, crack cocaine, and marijuana. The woman testified that she observed defendant selling drugs to various individuals. Defendant claimed that the woman did not have authority to consent to the search and filed a motion to suppress. On appeal, the court found that the officers had valid consent to search the room and that defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7 were not violated. The occupants in the room verified that the woman was staying in the room, and the officers smelled marijuana and observed the paraphernalia in plain sight. The officers reasonably believed that the woman had the authority to consent to the search. The evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction. Defendant was in a motel room with several other individuals who were smoking crack cocaine and marijuana, and witnesses testified that defendant supplied and sold drugs. The trial court properly considered the sentencing principles and did not err in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Morris v. State


No. W2005-00426-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 782


June 6, 2006, Session  
October 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Morris v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 202 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C01-50. John Franklin Murchison, Judge.
State v. Morris, 24 S.W.3d 788, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 391 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Circuit Court for Madison County (Tennessee) of two counts of premeditated first-degree murder and one count of aggravated rape and was sentenced to death. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to conduct an adequate investigation of petitioner's family background and mental condition, which precluded the diagnosis of a bipolar disorder. The court of appeals disagreed. While additional mitigation evidence existed in the form of additional information from family members and friends, the introduction of such information to the jury would not have all been beneficial mitigating evidence. The information highlighted a long history of drug abuse and illegal activity. Although such missing information would have been beneficial to a reviewing mental health expert, had the expert witness been in possession of such information he would not necessarily have made the same diagnosis, and the impact of such a diagnosis would not have had such effect upon the jury as to alter the outcome. Counsel was not deficient for relying upon the pre-trial evaluation finding that petitioner was competent and sane. In light of the results of the court-ordered evaluation, there would have most likely been no success in seeking additional funds to further explore an insanity defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

617 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carfi


No. M2005-01467-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 756


March 14, 2006, Session  
September 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Carfi, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 252 (Tenn., Mar. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Sumner County Criminal Court. No. 319-2002. Jane W. Wheatcraft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a former police officer, appealed from a judgment of the Sumner County Criminal Court (Tennessee) that convicted him of official misconduct under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-402, aggravated assault under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-102 and 39-11-402(2); and aggravated burglary under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-404(a); and that sentenced him to 15 years in prison as a Range I offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-402, and raised numerous claims of error. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but reversed his sentence because the record contained evidence of several mitigating factors but no indication that they were considered by the trial court. Also the trial court erred by applying the use of a deadly weapon enhancement factor to defendants' official misconduct and aggravated burglary convictions. The court found that defendant's convictions were supported by sufficient evidence that showed he had schemed with the other participants to attack the victim, and that the other participants entered the victim's home and beat him with a stick, which caused serious injures, while defendant used his police radio to ensure that no one called the police. The court held that § 39-16-402 was not unconstitutionally vague because it sufficiently put defendant on notice of the charges against him and of what conduct was prohibited. The court rejected defendant's claims of error as to hearsay or prior bad act evidence, the denial of pretrial diversion, and the State's election of offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but reversed defendant's sentence and remanded the case for new sentencing. Upon remand, the trial court was instructed to clearly indicate on the record the enhancing and mitigating factors that were applicable to each conviction.

State v. Bonds


No. M2005-02546-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 755


May 16, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
September 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Bonds v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 890 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2003-D-2670. Steven R. Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) convicting him of first-degree premeditated murder, felony murder, especially aggravated robbery, and two counts of aggravated burglary, and sentencing him to life in prison plus 28 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after his co-defendant shot the victim to death while he and defendant were stealing drugs and money from the victim's home. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant intentionally joined the codefendant in the venture and was thus criminally responsible for the victim's murder because: (1) an audiotape of defendant's conversation reflected that he anticipated having to kill the victim before the first burglary of the victim's apartment and that he was fine with that; (2) defendant stated that he and his codefendant were prepared to do whatever they had to do in order to carry out the second burglary of the victim's apartment; (3) defendant and his codefendant went into the victim's apartment armed; (4) they were aware that the victim was home and was probably armed before they attempted entry; (5) they waited until a lady they knew left the apartment because they did not want to put her in a bad situation; (6) defendant and the codefendant put a stolen ladder against the building and climbed up it into the victim's home; and (7) the codefendant shot the victim twice.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

McBee v. State


No. E2006-00097-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 661



August 29, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Pursuant to Rule 20, Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 83321. Ray Jenkins, Judge.
McBee v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1118 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 31, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner appealed the order of the Criminal Court for Knox County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief. The State filed a motion requesting that the court dismiss the appeal or affirm the denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: In December 1994, the jury convicted the petitioner for two counts of aggravated robbery. The trial court sentenced the petitioner to thirty years of imprisonment on each count and ordered the sentences to run consecutively for an effective sixty-year sentence. On November 18, 2005, the petitioner filed for post-conviction relief claiming that he received ineffective assistance of counsel at trial. The petition was filed more than seven years after the state supreme court denied permission to appeal. On December 9, 2005, the trial court dismissed the petition as barred by the one-year statute of limitations set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102. This was not a case in which due process considerations required that the statute of limitations be tolled. The petitioner did not explain his failure to timely to pursue post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in accordance with Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.

 

620 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arias


No. E2005-01700-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 644


May 16, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
August 9, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 243553. Douglas A. Meyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a) (2003), first-degree felony murder, attempted especially aggravated burglary, and theft of property valued over $ 10,000.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences, but the court affirmed, stating that the proof in his case did not support the lesser charge of voluntary manslaughter. There was no evidence introduced that defendant killed the victim in a state of passion produced by adequate provocation to lead a reasonable person to act in an irrational manner. And, even if it should have been charged, the failure to do was harmless. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for a change of venue under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 21 because the record contained no evidence from which the appellate court could conclude that the jurors were tainted. Defendant failed to prove that any pretrial publicity utterly corrupted the trial atmosphere. Pursuant to Tenn. R. Evid. 402, the trial court did not err in admitting a knife into evidence because it was relevant under Tenn. R. Evid. 401 to show where defendant might have obtained the murder weapon. The State was properly permitted to present a theory regarding the origin of the murder weapon and evidence to support that theory. Photographs were properly admitted to reconstruct the crime scene and were not overly graphic.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

621 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hawkins v. State


No. M2005-02807-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 588


June 20, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
July 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hawkins v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1216 (Tenn., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wayne County. No. 13811 & 13828. Robert Holloway, Judge.
Lofton v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 219 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 7, 1997)
Hawkins v. State, 1990 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 504 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 1, 1990)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellant petitioners challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Wayne County, Tennessee, dismissing their separate petitions for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The two petitioners were each found to be habitual criminals and, as a result, were serving sentences of life imprisonment in the Tennessee Department of Correction. On appeal, the petitioners argued that their habitual criminal convictions were illegal and void because Tennessee's habitual criminal statute was unconstitutional in its application. The petitioners alleged that the crimes for which they were convicted, and which resulted in their convictions as habitual criminals, occurred after the enactment of the Tennessee Sentencing Reform Act of 1982, and as such, they argued that they should have been sentenced as persistent offenders under the 1982 Act rather than under the habitual criminal statute. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's summary dismissal of the petitions. The Tennessee Sentencing Reform Act of 1982 contained the express provision that nothing in the Act would prohibit the operation of the Habitual Criminal Act. The Tennessee Legislature was within its authority to impose imprisonment beyond the maximum for the offense committed for those hardened offenders who had not been deterred from a life of crime by prior conviction and punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

State v. Johnson


No. E2005-00877-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 526


March 29, 2006, Session  
June 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Johnson, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 997 (Tenn., Oct. 30, 2006)
Appeal denied by State v. Johnson, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1057 (Tenn., Nov. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Entry of Corrected Judgments. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Campbell County. No. 11443. E. Shayne Sexton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Entry of Corrected Judgments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Campbell County (Tennessee), which convicted him of five counts of sexual battery, and five counts of aggravated sexual battery in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-504(a)(4) (2003). He was sentenced to one year for each sexual battery and eight years for each aggravated sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his five counts of sexual battery and five counts of aggravated sexual battery. The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court but remanded for entry of corrected judgments to reflect that Counts 3 and 5 were consecutive to Counts 1 and 2. Defendant not only failed to request any lesser-included offense instructions pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-18-110 (2003), he objected to the State's requested lesser-included instructions. He further failed to show that he did not waive that issue for tactical reasons and the trial court's failure to instruct on the lesser-included offenses did not rise to the level of plain error. Additionally, the trial court gave a proper unanimity instruction and any error in the jury instructions was harmless because the jury reached a proper verdict and the alternative convictions were properly merged by the trial court. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions because the victim's testimony revealed that defendant, her grandfather, toucher her breasts under her child. She also testified about numerous occasions wherein defendant sexually touched her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but remanded for entry of corrected judgments to reflect that Counts 3 and 5 were consecutive to Counts 1 and 2.

 

623 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Castile


No. M2004-02572-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 492


January 24, 2006, Session  
June 28, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 40200680. Michael R. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) of manufacturing methamphetamine, possession of methamphetamine with the intent to deliver, simple possession of methamphetamine, and criminal impersonation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying the motion to suppress because personal items were illegally seized as a result of the pat down which exceeded the scope of his consent. The court of appeals disagreed. The officers could have justified a warrantless search of the room based on the smell of methamphetamine alone based on the exigent circumstances created by the dangers associated with methamphetamine production. The officers arrived on the scene after reports of the smell of "ether" coming from defendant's room. When defendant opened the door and squeezed himself out, the officers could smell the strong chemical smell coming from the room. Defendant acted strange, telling them that he had come all the way from Florida with no wallet and no identification. While the officers procured a search warrant for the hotel room prior to their search which resulted in the discovery of a multitude of items used in the production of methamphetamine and some actual methamphetamine, they would have been justified in searching the room without a warrant based on the dangerous exigent circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Alley v. State


No. W2006-01179-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 470


June 19, 2006, Special Session  
June 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by Alley v. Tennessee, 126 S. Ct. 2975, 165 L. Ed. 2d 982, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5179 (U.S., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 85-05085-87. W. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
Alley v. Key, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 12882 (6th Cir. Tenn., May 14, 2006)
State v. Alley, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 683 (Tenn., June 2, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of aggravated rape, kidnapping, and first degree murder and was sentenced to death. After his request for postconviction DNA testing was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that the postconviction court erred by denying his petition to show that a third-party committed the murder. The court of appeals disagreed. While the petitioner placed great emphasis upon "redundant DNA results," the "redundant results" analysis did not differ from an individual determination as to the "favorable" nature of each item's DNA testing results. In essence, the crux of the petitioner's request for consideration of "redundant" test results was that the absence of the petitioner's DNA from the samples established his innocence of the murder. The Tennessee Post-Conviction DNA Analysis Act of 2001 did not envision DNA testing of third-party individuals nor did it contemplate a new investigation for a speculative phantom defendant. In addition, there was overwhelming evidence against the petitioner including his confession, his leading the police to the locale of the body, and the victim's hair found in the petitioner's vehicle. Therefore, the post-conviction court did not err by denying the petitioner's requested relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Keen v. State


No. W2004-02159-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 442


December 6, 2005, Session,  
June 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Keen v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1032 (Tenn., Oct. 30, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Keen v. Tennessee, 550 U.S. 938, 127 S. Ct. 2250, 167 L. Ed. 2d 1097, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 5243 (May 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-25157. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Keen, 31 S.W.3d 196, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 565 (Tenn., Oct. 5, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denying his petition for postconviction relief from his conviction of first-degree felony murder committed in the perpetration of a rape and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for killing the eight-year-old victim after raping her. On appeal, the court held that the fact that one juror read Bible passage aloud and another juror recited a prayer during deliberations during sentencing did not violate defendant's right to an impartial jury because they were not extraneous prejudicial information. A literal reading of the Bible passage showed that it did not mention imposition of the death penalty, or any other punishment related to murder, or any other specific crimes; its theme was that one should follow the laws of the civil government who rules. Given the victim's horrific murder, the court could not conclude that the typical juror would not have imposed the death penalty absent the reading of the Bible passage and/or the prayer. The court further held that the inmate failed to show that the postconviction court was biased, as his displeasure with the outcome of the hearing was insufficient, and that despite the inmate's argument to the contrary, the postconviction court considered all of the testimony presented, including mitigation evidence. The inmate's ineffective assistance of counsel claims were rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

Mayfield v. State


No. M2005-01988-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 419


March 14, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
May 31, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 88-F-1762; 89-W-222; IF-5635. Steve Dozier, Judge.
Mayfield v. Carlton, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 153 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 18, 2005)
State v. Mayfield, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 429 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 11, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denying his claim for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: On April 18, 2005, appellant filed a petition collaterally attacking his 1989 convictions for robbery and receiving stolen property. He alleged that the convictions were facially invalid and void due to the trial court's imposition of concurrent sentences. At the time of the appellant's 1989 convictions, the statute of limitations applicable to post-conviction proceedings was three years under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102 (1986) (repealed 1995). In order to comply with the statute of limitations, the appellant had until July 1992 to file for post-conviction relief. The post-conviction court summarily dismissed the petition as time-barred; he was not denied his right to due process of law because he had three years to file the petition. Appellant had previously sought and been denied habeas corpus relief. The post-conviction court did not err by refusing to treat the appellant's petition as one seeking habeas corpus relief. Appellant was incarcerated in Johnson County, Tennessee, while the post-conviction court was in Davidson County, Tennessee; therefore, jurisdiction was not proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

627 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Snowden


No. W2005-01851-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 383


April 11, 2006, Session  
May 11, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Appeal Dismissed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Gibson County. No. 7775. Clayburn Peeples, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Gibson County, Tennessee, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of a violation of the residency restriction for convicted sex offenders, a Class A misdemeanor. He received a sentence of eleven months and twenty-nine days, suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant complained that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment. The appellate court found that the judgment of conviction entered on July 28, 2005, failed to, by itself, properly reserve a certified question of law. It failed to incorporate by reference the plea agreement which set out defendant's certified question. The judgment of conviction instead incorporated by reference a subsequent order which was to set forth the parameters of defendant's certified question. Defendant filed his notice of appeal, and five days later, the trial court filed a supplemental order which purported to contain defendant's certified question. Once the notice of appeal was filed, the jurisdiction of the appellate court attached, and, correlatively, the trial court lost jurisdiction. Therefore, the attempt to cure the defect in the judgment with a supplemental order was a nullity. Even if the supplemental order had been filed in a timely fashion, it would not have served the dictates of Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37 as the wording did not clearly identify the scope or limits of the issue reserved and did not serve to properly reserve defendant's certified question.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Ross v. Turner

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 381

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Ross v. Turner, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 932 (Tenn., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County. No. 9752. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, denying his petition for habeas corpus relief. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court's denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered guilty pleas to facilitation of aggravated arson, assault, driving while declared a habitual motor vehicle offender, and escape. Petitioner received an effective twenty-year sentence in prison. He filed an application for writ of habeas corpus relief. The trial court found that the petition failed to allege any ground demonstrating that the judgment was void. Petitioner's assertion that his guilty plea was unknowing and involuntary and that the trial court failed to properly advise him regarding the nature of the offenses were not cognizable in a habeas corpus action. Even if true, the judgments would be rendered voidable, not void. Petitioner's claim that his convictions or sentences were void as he was sentenced in violation of Blakely did not render his judgment void. The trial court properly determined that petitioner had failed to establish his entitlement to habeas corpus relief under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in accordance with Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.

April 21, 2006, Filed

State v. Butler, 108 S.W.3d 845, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 573 (Tenn., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Circuit Court for Madison County (Tennessee) of driving under the influence of an intoxicant (DUI), fourth offense. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to prepare for trial adequately because he should have procured the surveillance tapes from a store, which he argued would have disputed the testimony of the arresting officer. The petitioner also claimed that his attorney did not prepare adequately for the testimony of certain witnesses. The court of appeals disagreed. In its order denying the petitioner postconviction relief, the trial court noted that the petitioner's attorney did not do anything to prejudice the petitioner. The record reflected that the store's surveillance tapes were reused before the petitioner's attorney was able to obtain them and that the petitioner's attorney adequately prepared for the trial. The record did not preponderate against the trial court's finding, and the petitioner was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Riels


No. W2004-02832-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 273


November 15, 2005, Session  
March 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Riels, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 142 (Tenn., Mar. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-06530. Chris Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentences of death imposed by the Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee after defendant pled guilty to first degree felony murder, first degree premeditated murder, attempted especially aggravated robbery, and aggravated burglary of the habitation of one victim, and first degree felony murder, first degree premeditated murder, and especially aggravated robbery of a second victim.


OVERVIEW: One victim was 89 years old and the other was a nurse. Officers became suspicious while questioning defendant, who had worked at the older victim's home. Defendant consented to a search and admitted killing the victims when bloody clothes were found. The court affirmed and held: (1) defendant's motion to suppress his statement was properly denied because he was advised of his Miranda rights, and he did not request a lawyer; (2) defendant voluntarily signed the consent to search as did his mother, and she supplied the officers with the clothing; (3) the ruling that defendant opened the door to cross-examination about the details of the offense because when he testified that he was remorseful was harmless error because the jury heard graphic testimony about the victims' injuries; (4) the photograph of the scene was relevant to depict the nature of the crimes; (5) the aggravating circumstance of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2) was proven by defendant's prior convictions of aggravated robbery; and (6) the § 39-13-204(i)(5) circumstance was shown by evidence of one victim being beaten in the head with a claw hammer, she had defensive wounds, and did not die immediately.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentences of death.

 

633 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dennis


No. M2005-00178-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 245


November 22, 2005, Session  
March 21, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Dennis, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 781 (Tenn., Aug. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County. No. 6776. Thomas W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Tennessee) of driving a motor vehicle while his blood alcohol concentration was .08 percent or more. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the police stop of his vehicle was not supported by probable cause or reasonable suspicion. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant was "seized" when the officer activated the blue lights following defendant's narrow miss of backing into the patrol car on the motel parking lot. At that point, the patrol car, with its blue lights on, was within feet of defendant's vehicle and partially blocking its exit from the parking space. Under those circumstances, a reasonable person would have believed that he was not free to leave. The officer's decision to make the investigatory stop was based upon reasonable suspicion supported by specific and articulable facts. The radio dispatch reported that a black Jeep traveling toward Monteagle with a Florida license place and identified tag number "was weaving all over the roadway." A vehicle generally matching that description was observed within minutes of the dispatch traveling toward Monteagle. The same vehicle nearly impacted the officer's patrol car on the motel parking lot. Those facts were sufficient to permit an investigative stop of defendant's vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Partin


No. E2004-02998-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 262


October 25, 2005, Session  
March 21, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Partin, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 493 (Tenn., May 30, 2006)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Partin v. Tennessee, 549 U.S. 1196, 127 S. Ct. 1240, 167 L. Ed. 2d 57, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1974 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Partin, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 295 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Campbell. County No. 11082. E. Shayne Sexton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Campbell County (Tennessee) of attempted first degree murder and two counts of aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress and the error was not harmless because the search warrant was based on negligent representations in the affidavit. The court of appeals disagreed. Although the information contained in the affidavit was insufficient to support a finding of probable cause because the affidavit was devoid of evidence linking the rifle to the shooting, the trial court's error in not suppressing the fired shell casings, fired bullets, or color photographs of defendant's residence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant's father purchased a MAK-90 rifle, which was a 7.62 by 39 caliber weapon and its instruction manual was entered as an exhibit and used by several witnesses to identify defendant's gun. A witness said that defendant used an AK-47 which looked like the gun in the booklet exhibit. An agent testified that the bullets and shell casings were 7.62 by 39 and could have been fired from a MAK-90 rifle, and a witness saw defendant with an assault rifle around the time the shooting occurred. Therefore, any error in the denial of the motion to suppress was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lewis


No. M2004-02255-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 237


November 22, 2005, Session  
March 15, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, April 24, 2006.
Appeal denied by State v. Lewis, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 857 (Tenn., Sept. 25, 2006)
Affirmed by State v. Lewis, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 649 (Tenn., Aug. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-B-713. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of criminally negligent homicide and facilitation of attempted especially aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court improperly allowed her statement to be admitted into evidence. The court of appeals disagreed. The police went to defendant's residence, knocked on the door, and invited her to come give a statement regarding the incident at the antique store. Defendant voluntarily gave the statement and was free to leave at any time. Defendant admitted that she was in the antique store at around 9:30 a.m. on the day of the murder, that the victim paid her $ 125 in cash for the two vases and that, after leaving the store, she returned the car she borrowed and went to her mother's house. Although she specifically denied any involvement with or participation in the attempted robbery or murder, she responded positively to questions, which, when considered along with the victim's dying declaration and the identification of defendant as the driver of the getaway car, tended to establish the her guilt. The trial court properly admitted defendant's video-taped statement as an admission against interest under Tenn. R. Evid. 803(1.2)(A).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Shaw v. State


No. W2005-01332-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 204



March 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Shaw v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 748 (Tenn., Aug. 21, 2006)
Appeal denied by Shaw v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 803 (Tenn., Aug. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 93-08189; 93-08190. W. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
Shaw v. State, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 493 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denied petitioner inmate's motion requesting relief from an invalid sentence. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Retrospective application of the rule in Blakely to cases on collateral review was not required. Accordingly, the inmate failed to establish a ground that would toll the statute of limitations. The inmate had filed prior petitions for post-conviction relief; thus, the appellate court could construe the pleading as a motion to reopen a petition for post-conviction relief. However, even treating the pleading as such, it failed. The appeal failed as the inmate had not satisfied the procedural requirements for vesting jurisdiction in the appellate court. The appeal was not filed within 10 days of the trial court's ruling, no application for permission to appeal was filed, and the notice of appeal was filed in the trial court, not the appellate court. Also, the inmate failed to allege a ground under which a petition for post-conviction relief could be reopened. Further, the claims regarding sentencing were voidable, not void, and the Blakely holding was not to be applied retroactively. In addition, if treated as an application for habeas corpus relief, the application was filed in the wrong court. Thus, the inmate failed to establish that he was entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal.

Adams v. State

2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 176

Appeal denied by Adams v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 762 (Tenn., Aug. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-22151. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Adams, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1247 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 11, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied his motion to reopen his postconviction petition.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of felony murder and two counts of attempted felony murder, with the latter being reversed and dismissed. In November 1999, he filed a petition for postconviction relief, which, according to the inmate, was dismissed for failure to prosecute. Additionally, he alleged that the court denied, on January 25, 2002, his motion to reconsider the dismissal. On January 19, 2005, he filed a motion to reopen his postconviction petition. The only "facts" alleged by the inmate was that a ballistics report would have proven that he did not shoot anyone or had a weapon used in the crime. Such findings would have been contrary to the facts that were the basis of the inmate's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Reeves v. State


No. M2004-02642-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 143


October 26, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
February 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Reeves v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 477 (Tenn., May 30, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Reeves v. Brandon, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14209 (M.D. Tenn., Feb. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2001-C-1889. Steve Dozier, Judge.
State v. Reeves, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 732 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief by the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee. Following a jury trial, petitioner was convicted of two counts of aggravated child abuse.


OVERVIEW: There was testimony that when the victim was four or five years old, defendant choked him with a dog leash and spanked him with a board. Petitioner maintained that he was out of town when the incidents were alleged to have occurred, and counsel testified that he focused on the alibi as a defense. The court affirmed and held that counsel was not ineffective for not objecting to the victim's competency because the victim's confusion over details did not address his competency but went to the weight and value of his testimony. Petitioner also failed to show that counsel's cross-examination of witnesses was deficient in that counsel cross-examined the victim's grandmother at length about conflicting statements and counsel's cross-examination of the officer was reasonable in light of counsel's trial strategy. The court also found that counsel's inability to secure telephone records petitioner claimed would show petitioner was in a different area when the injuries allegedly occurred did not reflect deficient conduct. Further, counsel believed that interviewing the doctor prior to trial was unnecessary given that the trial strategy was based on petitioner's alibi defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the post-conviction court.

 

639 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Noble


No. E2005-00011-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 155


September 27, 2005, Session  
February 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by State v. Noble, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 216 (Tenn., Mar. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 67847. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) dismissing a presentment charging defendant with the rape of a five-year-old child at a day care under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-522. Following a mistrial, the State filed a "Superceding Bill of Particulars," which reverted back to the general time frame of the presentment.


OVERVIEW: The State based the times of the offense in the bill of particulars on the day care's attendance records. After the mistrial, the State's superseding bill of particulars broadened the time in which the offense occurred because the defense provided new evidence during discovery that suggested that the child arrived at day care 35 minutes earlier than the time alleged in the bill of particulars. The court reversed, and held that given that there was no clearly defined procedure in Tenn. R. Crim. P. 7(b) for amending a bill of particulars, the fact that the State did not file a motion for permission to supercede the bill did not result in the issues being waived on appeal. The original bill set out its allegations as to when the offense took place but were not admissions as to the accuracy of allegations of fact made by defendant. Finally, the court held that there was no question of defense counsel's having been surprised by the time discrepancy, and "prejudice," did not occur simply because defendant lost an advantage earlier gained from a prosecution mistake. The appropriate action would have been to determine whether the variance was both material and prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the presentment and remanded.

State v. Holladay


No. E2004-02858-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 152


August 16, 2005, Session  
February 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 22, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Case Dismissed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Anderson County. No. A4CR0044. James B. Scott, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Case Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Anderson County, Tennessee, indicted defendant for one count of vehicular homicide by intoxication, a Class B felony, and one count of vehicular homicide by recklessness, a Class C felony. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred in granting defendant's motion to suppress. It claimed that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the equipment or safety features of defendant's vehicle. The appellate court noted that it did not believe the statement in the notice of appeal constituted evidence of the fact asserted. The State actually suppressed only the evidence obtained by the tapping of the internal record contained in the computer module. Because the air bag sensor module would not show defendant was under the influence of an intoxicant or had a blood alcohol concentration of .08% or higher, the first count of the indictment charging vehicular homicide by intoxication had to have been based on evidence in addition to the air bag sensor module. The State's assertion in its notice of appeal was not supported by the record. Nothing in the record existed to indicate that the suppression of the information taken from the air bag sensor module effectively resulted in the dismissal of either count of the indictment. The State failed to establish any factors allowing a Tenn. R. App. P. 10 extraordinary appeal.


OUTCOME: The State's appeal was dismissed.
