State v. Swader


No. M2005-00185-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 109


September 21, 2005, Session  
February 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Swader, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 576 (Tenn., June 26, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Swader v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 854 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 7, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. F-54010. James K. Clayton, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee) of first degree felony murder, second degree murder, attempted especially aggravated robbery, and possession of a deadly weapon during the commission of an offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions because no evidence, other than his proximity to the victim, corroborated his statement that he intended to rob someone. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant told an officer that on the night of the shooting, he was in an apartment complex and near the G building. A witness was ninety to ninety-five percent certain that the male she gave a cigarette to near that building was defendant. Defendant told the police that at the time of the shooting, he was standing in the parking lot and the victim was standing near the sidewalk. Another witness testified that when he first saw the victim, she was lying partially on the sidewalk, and a shell casing was found in the parking lot. Defendant said the gun was a nine millimeter, and an officer testified that the shell casing recovered from the crime scene was a nine millimeter. Defendant told police that he shot the victim as the victim turned away from him, and the evidence showed that the victim was shot in the back. Therefore, defendant's confession was sufficiently corroborated by other evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Studdard v. State


No. W2005-02707-CCA-RM-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 114


November 30, 2005, Remanded by Supreme Court  
February 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Studdard v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 752 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 27, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Studdard v. Tennessee, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8148 (U.S., Oct. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dyer County. No. C02-61. Lee Moore, Judge.
Studdard v. State, 182 S.W.3d 283, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1046 (Tenn., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court for Dyer County, Tennessee, the defendant pled guilty to one count of incest, a Class C felony, in exchange for a negotiated eight-year sentence as a Range II, multiple offender. The Tennessee Supreme Court concluded that the trial court had jurisdiction to accept the defendant's guilty plea and remanded the case to the intermediate appellate court for consideration of the defendant's sentencing issues.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a Tenn. R. Crim. P. 35 pro se motion for reduction of sentence, seeking relief from his eight-year sentence for incest. Defendant alleged, inter alia, that he did not timely learn that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-503(c) required him to obtain certification from a psychiatrist that he would not commit further sexual assaults before he could be released on parole. He challenged the statute on equal protection grounds under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The intermediate appellate court held that he was not entitled to relief. It was reasonable for the legislature to treat sexual offenders differently based on the nature of their offenses and its concerns for public safety. The fact that the defendant did not learn of the sexual offender requirements for parole until after sentencing, and that his mother's health had deteriorated since the time of his guilty plea, did not permit modification of his sentence in the interest of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Wright v. State


No. M2005-02284-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 104

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. Nos. F-47083 & F-47349. Don R. Ash, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from the dismissal by the Circuit Court for Rutherford County, Tennessee, of his petition for post-conviction relief. The State filed a motion pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20 and requested that the dismissal be affirmed.


OVERVIEW: On June 17, 1999, the inmate pled guilty to attempted rape and failure to appear. The trial court sentenced the inmate to ten years for the attempted rape conviction and four years for the failure to appear conviction, and it ordered that these sentences run consecutively for an effective sentence of fourteen years. On July 15, 2005, the inmate filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief, which the post-conviction court dismissed after finding that the petition was untimely. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's petition because Tenn. Additionally, the inmate did not meet any of the exceptions to the limitation period set forth in § 40-30-102(b)(1)- (3). Additionally, as Blakely v. Washington did not provide a new rule of constitutional law, it did not provide a basis for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the inmate's petition and State's motion were affirmed.

Parrish v. Mills


No. W2005-02196-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 78



January 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Parrish v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 419 (Tenn., May 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5992. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appeals the denial of his petition for habeas corpus relief by the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee). The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of aggravated burglary, one count of theft of property valued over $ 1,000 but less than $ 10,000, and one count of aggravated robbery. For those convictions, the inmate received an effective sentence of 15 years' incarceration. He filed an application for habeas corpus relief. The inmate did not contend that his sentences had expired; thus, he was only entitled to relief if his judgments were void. In his petition submitted to the trial court, the inmate challenged the voluntary nature of his guilty pleas and the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-501(l)(2). The appellate court held that those claims did not entitle the inmate to habeas corpus relief. First, the inmate's assertion that his guilty plea was unknowing and involuntary was not cognizable in a habeas corpus action because even if true the judgment would be rendered voidable, not void. Next, the inmate's constitutional challenge to § 40-35-501(l)(2) failed because there was no constitutional or inherent right to be conditionally released before the expiration of a prison sentence. Thus, the inmate failed to state a ground upon which habeas corpus relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Dotson v. State


No. M2005-00436-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 95


December 20, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
January 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal allowed by, Remanded by Dotson v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 129 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 3619. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his pro se petition for writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner argued that he was entitled to habeas corpus relief because his sentences contravened Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-111(b) and Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32(c)(3)(C). He also alleged that his sentences were unconstitutionally enhanced in violation of his right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to one count of aggravated assault and two counts of attempted first degree murder. He was sentenced to three years for his aggravated assault conviction and 20 years for each of his attempted first degree murder convictions. His sentences were ordered to run concurrently. In his petition, he alleged that he was on bail from the aggravated assault charge at the time he committed the two offenses of attempted first degree murder. Therefore, he argued that his concurrent sentences were illegal and void because § 40-20-111(b) and Rule 32(c)(3)(C) mandated consecutive sentencing under such circumstances. On appeal, the court determined that the habeas corpus court should not have dismissed his claims without the benefit of counsel or a hearing. It noted that if petitioner's allegations were proven, then his sentences were void and he was entitled to habeas corpus relief. The court also determined that petitioner's claim that his sentences were improperly enhanced in violation of his right to a jury trial was waived because he failed to present it in his habeas corpus petition and could not raise it for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

648 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Parker


No. M2005-01924-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 29



January 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Gardner v. Parker, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 468 (Tenn., May 30, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gardner v. Parker, 549 U.S. 1060, 127 S. Ct. 677, 166 L. Ed. 2d 528, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 9139 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 97-D-2814. Monte Watkins, Judge.
State v. Gardner, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 239 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 30, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, summarily dismissed petitioner inmate's petition for writ of habeas corpus. The State filed a motion for the appellate court to affirm the judgment of the trial court pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-109, the trial court could dismiss a petition for writ of habeas corpus without conducting an evidentiary hearing if the trial court found, on the face of the petition, that the applicant was not entitled to relief. The inmate's contention that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 was unconstitutional because it violated Tenn. Code art. II, § 17 was without merit. The constitutional provision applied to legislative bills which were introduced for adoption by the General Assembly. Codification of legislative enactments cured all defects in the caption of a bill. The remaining issues raised by the inmate, even if true, would render the judgment voidable and not void.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

649 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mann v. State


No. W2005-02453-CCA-R28-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1032



January 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mann v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 509 (Tenn., May 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Circuit Court for Dyer County. No. C93-337-338.
Mann v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 858 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 9, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate applied for permission to appeal a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dyer County (Tennessee) denying his motion to reopen his postconviction petition, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-117(c), challenging his convictions of first-degree murder, aggravated rape, and aggravated burglary.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for burglarizing, raping, and killing the 62-year-old victim. On review, the court held that the inmate failed to allege a ground under which his petition for postconviction relief could be reopened and therefore affirmed the trial court's judgment. The inmate's claim of newly discovered evidence establishing that co-counsel had a conflict of interest failed to satisfy any of the three circumscribed grounds as provided in § 40-30-117(a)(1-3), and due process did not create a fourth category under which the inmate could reopen his petition. The inmate's claim that the Deck v. Missouri case created a new rule of constitutional law warranting postconviction relief was rejected because retrospective application of the procedural rule announced in that case was not required, because the rule, while important for defendants, was not absolute for defendants. The case pronounced that routine shackling during the penalty phase of a capital trial, without a case-specific finding that security needs justified the shackling, violated a defendant's due process rights unless the State showed beyond a reasonable doubt that the shackling did not contribute to the verdict.


OUTCOME: The inmate's application for permission to appeal was denied and the judgment denying his motion to reopen his postconviction petition was affirmed.

 

650 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Mills


No. W2005-01587-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1308



December 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5958. Joe H. Walker, Judge.
Taylor v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 534 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 30, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Lauderdale County, Tennessee, denied petitioner inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the inmate failed to satisfy the procedural requirements for habeas corpus relief and that the criminal court had jurisdiction to sentence defendant to the sentence that he received and that the sentence had not expired. The appellate court noted that the inmate failed to attach copies of the judgments of conviction to his petition for habeas corpus relief filed in the trial court. The procedural requirements for habeas corpus relief were mandatory and had to be scrupulously followed. An application for the issuance of the writ of habeas corpus could be summarily dismissed for the failure to attach the judgment forms, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107(b)(2). The inmate did not contend that his sentences had expired; thus, he was only entitled to relief if his judgments were void. The inmate's claim that his convictions or sentences were void because he was sentenced in violation of Blakely failed as, even if such a violation had occurred, the violation would only render the judgment voidable, not void. The inmate was statutorily time-barred from seeking post-conviction relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the State's motion was granted.

 

651 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Meeks v. Bell


No. M2005-00626-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1286



December 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Motion denied by Meeks v. Bell, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 379 (Tenn., May 1, 2006)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Meeks v. Bell, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1991 (U.S., Feb. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 04C-3157. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
Meeks v. State, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 176 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 3, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate had been convicted in the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, for aggravated kidnapping, especially aggravated robbery, especially aggravated burglary, and extortion. Subsequently, he filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, which was summarily dismissed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In four allegations supporting grounds for relief, the inmate's petition generally alleged that his convictions were void because he was sentenced by a judge rather than by a jury and that his sentences were enhanced by a judge rather than a jury, in violation of his constitutional rights under both the federal and state constitutions for a trial by jury. The fifth allegation as a ground for relief was essentially an argument of law, which the appellate court found was contrary to well-established case law in Tennessee. With regard to the first four allegations, the appellate court held that under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-21-101 et seq., a habeas corpus petition could only be used to contest void judgments which were facially invalid because the convicting court was without jurisdiction or authority to sentence a defendant or if a petitioner's sentence had expired. The appellate court concluded that the inmate failed to provide any evidence to suggest that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to convict or sentence him, and the record was clear that his term of imprisonment had not yet expired; therefore, he was properly denied habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

652 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. State


No. W2004-00914-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1282


June 7, 2005, Session  
December 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Burns v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 362 (Tenn., Apr. 24, 2006)
Appeal denied by Burns v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 727 (Tenn., Sept. 29, 2008)
Appeal denied by Burns v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 83 (Tenn., Jan. 23, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-21820. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Burns, 979 S.W.2d 276, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 666 (Tenn., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of two counts of felony murder and two counts of attempted felony murder. The petitioner was sentenced to death. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel were ineffective because they failed to present significant mitigation evidence. The court of appeals disagreed. Counsel conducted an investigation and developed a mitigation theory to which they adhered. The testimony of the witnesses at the sentencing hearing supported counsel's investigation and development of the theory. Based on their investigation, counsel determined that the best mitigation defense was to show that the petitioner was "a good guy" and that the crime was out of character for him, that theory based upon the information provided by the petitioner and his family. There was no indication, by either the petitioner or his parents, that further investigation into the family history was necessary or would have been fruitful. Although much information specific to the petitioner's mother and father and not directly related to him was presented at the post-conviction hearing, that proof shadowed the mitigation theme of the defense at trial, i.e., that the petitioner was "a good guy." Counsels' decision not to further investigate into the petitioner's background was reasonable based upon the information they had.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Porterfield v. State


No. W2005-00549-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1274


October 4, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
December 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Porterfield v. Bell, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 732 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 85-01174. W. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
Porterfield v. Tennessee, 541 U.S. 942, 124 S. Ct. 1668, 158 L. Ed. 2d 367, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2134 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. He previously pursued an unsuccessful motion for post-conviction relief. He filed a habeas corpus petition asserting several claims regarding the validity of his sentence. He was not truthful about the number of petitions he had previously filed. Despite his failure to comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107, the trial court issued a ruling on the issues in the habeas petition. A jury imposed the sentence of death; therefore, Blakely did not apply. While petitioner claimed that his simple robbery convictions were not violent felonies as contemplated by the sentencing statute, the error did not render his sentences void. Because his sentence was not facially invalid, he was not entitled to habeas relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

654 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collins


No. M2004-02564-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1259


July 20, 2005, Session  
December 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Collins, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 387 (Tenn., May 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2003-T-251. Monte Watkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of driving under the influence (DUI) and DUI per se. The trial court found that defendant had three previous DUI convictions and sentenced him for DUI, fourth offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. That defendant was driving a motor vehicle, and on a public road, were uncontroverted. Defendant contended in his brief that there was insufficient evidence presented to prove element three, that he was under the influence of an intoxicant. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, it established that the police responded to an accident involving defendant, and upon arriving at the scene the police questioned defendant, who smelled of alcohol and admitted that he had been drinking earlier in the day. The police officer on the scene subsequently administered two separate field sobriety tests, neither of which defendant completed successfully. Thereafter, defendant was placed under arrest and given a blood alcohol test, which showed that his blood alcohol content was .12, which was above the legal limit. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find the essential elements of DUI and DUI per se beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

655 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


DuBose v. Parker


No. W2005-01320-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1263


October 4, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
December 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Dubose v. Parker, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 739 (Tenn., Aug. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County. No. 05-CR-9705. R. Lee Moore, Jr., Judge.
DuBose v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 141 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Circuit Court for Lake County (Tennessee) of first-degree murder. After the petitioner's motion for writ of habeas corpus was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that the postconviction court erred by denying his petition for writ of habeas corpus because his indictment was invalid as it failed to state an offense. The court of appeals disagreed. The indictment provided sufficient information to: (1) put the petitioner on notice as to the charge against which he must defend; (2) furnish the trial court with adequate basis for the entry of a proper judgment; and (3) protect the petitioner from double jeopardy. Under such circumstances, even an indictment that failed to allege the required mental state was still valid. The petitioner's indictment tracked both the language of the statute proscribing first degree murder of a child by aggravated child abuse, and the language of the relevant child abuse statutes. Furthermore, the indictment cited to the first degree murder statute, and that reference provided notice to the petitioner of the applicable mens rea, notice of the offense upon which to enter the judgment, and protection from subsequent prosecution on the same offense. Moreover, the indictment complied with the statutory form requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-13-202.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Penny v. State


No. E2004-01735-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1255


September 27, 2005, Session  
December 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Penny v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 233 (Tenn., Mar. 27, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Penny v. Tennessee, 549 U.S. 826, 127 S. Ct. 350, 166 L. Ed. 2d 44, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5910 (Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 130199, 248876. Douglas A. Meyer, Judge.
United States v. Penney, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25560 (E.D. Tenn., May 14, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) denied defendant's motion for a corrected judgment and his petition for post-conviction relief arguing that his 1976 judgment should be corrected pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36 and that his post-conviction petition was not time-barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: In 1976 defendant believed he pled guilty to a misdemeanor, but the judgment showed he pled guilty to a felony. He petitioned to correct his sentence under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36 and for post-conviction relief. The court denied relief, finding no clerical error and that the post-conviction relief claims were untimely. After considering if there were any grounds for sua sponte habeas relief, the court concluded that neither the conviction nor sentence was illegal. Defendant appealed. The denial of a Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36 motion to correct a judgment for a clerical error was not covered by Tenn. R. App. P. 3, so defendant did not have an appeal as of right. Even accepting that he had a right to appeal the denial of his motion, the records showed he pled guilty to a felony. Defendant sought post-conviction relief for a judgment that was executed almost 30 years ago. The court dismissed the petition as being barred by a three-year statute of limitations. Defendant's claim that his 1976 judgment was illegal was essentially a claim for habeas relief. The instant court found he was not being restrained of his liberty under the 1976 judgment and, thus, not entitled to habeas relief.


OUTCOME: The order of the post-conviction court was affirmed.

State v. Hawkins


No. E2004-01761-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1161


June 28, 2005, Session  
November 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hawkins, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 244 (Tenn., Mar. 27, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hawkins v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Case Remanded for Entry of a Corrected Judgment. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S46,562. Phyllis H. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Case Remanded for Entry of a Corrected Judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first degree premeditated murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1) (2003), and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after he was convicted and sentenced for first degree premeditated murder. He challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, the trial court's evidentiary rulings, and the jury instructions. The court affirmed however, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The evidence established that defendant had two friends drive him to the victim's camper and told them to wait for him at a nearby church. Defendant returned to his friends' van a short time later with blood on his face, saying that he had left the victim for dead and that it was gruesome. Moreover, there was evidence that defendant had been upset with the victim and angry that the victim had called him a "snitch." Defendant conceded that proof of the victim's displeasure with defendant was introduced through other witnesses. Therefore, even if the trial court erred in excluding the calls in question, such error was harmless pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 52(a) and Tenn. R. App. P. 36(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but remanded to the trial court for an entry of a corrected judgment to reflect the correct date of the judgment.

 

658 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Parker


No. W2005-00384-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1160



October 27, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County No. 04-CR-8634. R. Lee Moore, Jr., Judge. Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 
State v. Jackson, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 956 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 26, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus relief in the Circuit Court for Lake County (Tennessee) attacking the validity of his Montgomery County convictions for one count of evading arrest by motor vehicle, one count of theft of property over $ 1,000, one count of kidnapping, two counts of aggravated robbery, and one count of aggravated assault. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the petition failed to comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107(a). Petitioner failed to state whether the legality of the restraint had not already been adjudged upon a prior proceeding of the same character. Additionally, he failed to state whether the instant petition was his first application for the writ, or, if a previous application had been made, and he failed to attach a copy of the petition and proceedings thereon. Accordingly, the petition was properly dismissed for failure to comply with the procedural requirements. In addition for failing to comply with the statutory requirements, petitioner failed to file a petition that stated cognizable claims for habeas corpus relief. Again, he made various complaints, including that: (1) counsel was ineffective; (2) his guilty plea was involuntarily; (3) he was innocent; (4) the Department of Correction unconstitutionally altered his sentences; (5) the trial court unconstitutionally imposed fines; and (6) the sentences were imposed in violation of Blakely v. Washington. Those claims did not, even if proven, render the convictions void. Thus, the claims were not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Yates v. State


No. W2005-01047-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1139


October 4, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
October 25, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5022. Joseph H. Walker, Judge.
Yates v. Sundquist, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 626 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 9, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a pro se pleading seeking to have a conviction and sentence set aside as unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Lauderdale County, Tennessee, treated the pleading as seeking a writ of habeas corpus and summarily denied the petitioner's claim for relief. The petitioner appealed as of right.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted and sentenced to life imprisonment for open rebellion, concurrent sentences of nine years for aggravated assault offenses, and eleven months twenty-nine days for simple assault. The petitioner filed pro se a pleading claiming that his sentence was void. The petitioner claimed that his conviction for open rebellion was void on the bases that his life sentence violated the Blakely decision. The trial court summarily dismissed the petitioner's claim for relief. Blakely did not apply retroactively. There was nothing on the face of the record before the court to indicate that the petitioner's sentence was imposed in direct contravention of any statute. The statute of limitations for filing a post-conviction claim on the petitioner's conviction of open rebellion had long since passed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102 (Supp. 1986).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

660 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Black v. State


No. M2004-01345-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1129


July 19, 2005, Session  
October 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Black v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 144 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Black v. Tenn., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6678 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 88-S-1479. Walter J. Kurtz, Judge.
State v. Black, 815 S.W.2d 166, 1991 Tenn. LEXIS 322 (Tenn., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of three counts of first degree murder. After his request for postconviction relief was denied the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in finding that he was not mentally retarded and thus eligible for the death penalty. The court of appeals disagreed. Although the petitioner's experts maintained that his mental retardation was a result of his mother's drinking of alcohol while she was pregnant, the proof in the record did not support that the petitioner's I.Q. was below seventy or that he had deficits in his adaptive behavior prior to age eighteen. Language, reading, writing, money concepts, and self-direction were the four basic areas examined to determine if there is a deficit in the conceptual area of adaptive functioning. A State's expert found that the petitioner had age appropriate functioning within the conceptual category and his social skills were intact and at or above the level suggested by measures of intellectual functioning. The expert concluded that the petitioner had no practical deficits in his activities of daily living. Accordingly, the petitioner did not meet the third prong of the test for mental retardation. Because the petitioner failed to prove that he was mentally retarded, he was not excluded from the sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Anderson v. Mills


No. W2005-01403-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1121



October 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5964. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of second degree murder. He was sentenced to thirty (30) years confinement in the state penitentiary. He filed a habeas corpus petition, which was denied by the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County, Tennessee. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a habeas corpus petition. As grounds for relief, he complained that he was being illegally restrained by the parole board in violation of their parole guidelines. The trial court properly denied the petition. Petitioner did not have a protected liberty interest in parole. Actions by the parole board were reviewable by the common law writ of certiorari, and had to be filed in chancery court pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-9-102. Petitioner's challenge to the actions of the parole board was not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Vasques


No. M2004-00166-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1100


March 8, 2005, Session  
October 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Vasques, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 140 (Tenn., Feb. 27, 2006)
Affirmed by State v. Vasques, 221 S.W.3d 514, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 243 (Tenn., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Alonzo v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 678 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 30, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hernandez v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 927 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2000-D-1876. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of conspiracy to possess with intent to sell more than seventy pounds of marijuana within one thousand feet of a school zone. The trial court thereafter granted defendants' petitions for coram nobis relief and vacated defendants' convictions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in granting coram nobis relief to defendants because there was sufficient evidence to convict each defendant even in the absence of the illegal conduct by an agent of stealing cocaine from the crime lab. The court of appeals disagreed as to two of the defendants. The agent directly implicated two of the defendants in the conspiracy. Although another officer observed defendants when they parked next to him, his testimony reflected that they were only parked for one to two minutes before leaving. The agent's role in the investigation and prosecution of the case was vital in obtaining convictions against defendants. The trial found that had the information regarding the agent's criminal acts and drug addiction been available to defendants, he could have been cross-examined regarding his drug use and criminal acts, his credibility could have been attacked, and alternate defenses might have been employed. A reasonable jury, informed of the agent's drug use and criminal acts, might have chosen to reject all or part of his testimony.


OUTCOME: The trial court's coram nobis judgment was affirmed as to two defendants but was reversed as to four defendants. The convictions of four of the defendants were affirmed.

Stephens v. Bell


No. M2004-02820-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1087


June 21, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
October 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Stephens v. Bell, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 162 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 96-C-1248. Seth Norman, Judge.
Stephens v. State, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1114 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of aggravated rape and sentenced to twenty years in prison. The Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied his petition for habeas corpus relief. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a habeas appeal, petitioner alleged that the judgment convicting him of aggravated rape was void because his sentence was imposed by the trial judge, rather than a jury. The habeas court properly denied relief. The 1989 Sentencing Act (Tennessee) did not violate constitutional protections, because the Blakely decision did not apply retroactively. Petitioner failed to prove that his sentence was facially void so as to warrant habeas relief under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Grimes v. Dotson


No. W2005-00862-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1083



October 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Grimes v. Dotson, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 281 (Tenn., Mar. 27, 2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Grimes v. Parker, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 24 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County No. R.D. 05-02-0023. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.
Grimes v. State, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1067 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 15, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate convicted of rape, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, denying his petition for habeas corpus relief. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court's denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20. The petitioner failed to allege any ground that would render the judgment of conviction void.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner entered guilty pleas to three counts of rape, class B felonies. For these offenses, the trial court imposed an effective sentence of twenty years confinement. Petitioner was also classified a multiple rapist, requiring one hundred percent service of his sentence. He filed for habeas relief, claiming that his criminal sentence was unconstitutionally enhanced in violation of his right to a jury trial as proscribed by Blakely. The petitioner's claim was not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding. Even if he was sentenced in violation of Blakely, this would only render the judgment voidable, not void. The claim could have been raised in a petition for post-conviction relief; however, the petitioner was time-barred from seeking relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

665 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graves


No. E2004-02620-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1073


June 29, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
October 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation March 27, 2006.
Appeal denied by State v. Graves, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 234 (Tenn., Mar. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Resentencing. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Loudon County. No. 10100. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Criminal Court for Loudon County (Tennessee) of theft of property. The petitioner filed an appeal from the order granting her postconviction relief, which allowed a delayed appeal, and from the order denying her amended motion for judgment of acquittal or, alternatively, a new trial. The State cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying her amended motion for judgment of acquittal, or alternatively, a new trial based on ineffective assistance of counsel. The State argued that the claim was not properly before the court of appeals because the petitioner was granted a delayed appeal and the trial court lost jurisdiction to hear the motion once the petitioner filed her notice of appeal. The court of appeals agreed with the State. The statute clearly did not allow both a delayed appeal and a motion for a new trial. Here, the trial court granted a delay appeal. As such, the petitioner was not also entitled to thirty days in which to file a motion for a new trial, and the trial court did not err in not granting such. The State, having been granted leave to appeal the petitioner's sentence, was free to file its notice of appeal when it did. Consequently, only the claims related to the petitioner's delayed appeal were properly before the court of appeals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

666 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pickett


No. M2004-00732-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1076


March 9, 2005, Argued  
October 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Pickett, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 139 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)
Affirmed by State v. Pickett, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 10 (Tenn., Jan. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-C-1439. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of eleven counts of sexual exploitation of a minor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the State failed to prove separate and distinct violations of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003 and that his eleven convictions were multiplicitous. The court of appeals agreed. The indictment alleged that defendant committed the offenses between January 1 and July 13, 2002, and the State introduced into evidence a computer printout showing which websites defendant visited from May 20 to June 13, 2002. The printout also showed the dates and times defendant visited the websites. However, the State presented no evidence concerning which pictures came from which website or when defendant accessed each picture. A detective admitted that he could not determine which pictures came from which website and could not determine when the petitioner accessed each picture. Therefore, all of the pictures could have come from a single website and could have been automatically downloaded onto defendant's hard drive simultaneously. In other words, the State failed to prove that any time elapsed between accessing the pictures or that defendant formed a new intent as to each picture.


OUTCOME: Ten counts were reversed. The sentence was modified. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

667 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Griffin


No. W2003-01636-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1070


July 12, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
September 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Griffin, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 230 (Tenn., Mar. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-10130. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.
State v. Griffin, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1063 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 11, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of aggravated assault and felony evading arrest. The trial court set aside the aggravated assault conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was prejudiced by the trial court's failure to charge Class E evading arrest as a lesser-included offense of Class D evading arrest. The court of appeals disagreed. Clearly the jury determined that defendant "intentionally or knowingly" committed an assault and acted in such a way as to create a "risk of death or injury" to another person. Despite the fact that the trial court opted to set aside the conviction for aggravated assault, it was apparent from the verdict that the jury believed that defendant created a "risk of death or injury." The State proved that the trial court's failure to instruct on Class E felony evading arrest did not affect the outcome of the trial. Under those circumstances, the jury, if given the option of Class E felony evading arrest, would not have abandoned its findings of a risk to third parties and convicted only of the Class E crime. Therefore, the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on Class E felony evading arrest was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

668 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Kelley v. State


No. M2004-01158-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1016


March 8, 2005, Session  
September 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Kelley v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 174 (Tenn., Feb. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Wilson County. No. 99-1455. John D. Wootten, Jr., Judge.
State v. Kelley, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 424 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 7, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the order from the Criminal Court for Wilson County (Tennessee), which denied his post-conviction petition, wherein he sought relief from judgments convicting him of one count of premeditated first degree murder and one count of murder committed in the perpetration of or attempt to perpetrate aggravated child abuse.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner smothered his baby, and she died. He told police that God had directed him to sacrifice his daughter. He signed a statement, which was read into evidence at trial, stating that he killed his child so that Christ could return. He was convicted. A panel of the court affirmed the judgment on direct appeal. He unsuccessfully sought post-conviction relief based on the absence of a jury instruction on the term "wrongfulness," as used in an insanity defense. On appeal, he requested that the court define the term as suggested in the Graham court's opinion. The court found that the merit of the jury instruction issue was addressed on direct appeal when the court found that the instructions were complete. As such, the court found that the issue was precluded from its review under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(h) (2003). Further, the court found that absent any established definition of wrongfulness, petitioner's defense counsel properly relied on experts to provide explanations on various definitions and to opine as to why petitioner met the standards of the insanity defense. The court found that the fact that the strategy failed did not establish ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief.

 

669 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hood


No. W2004-01678-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1008



September 13, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-05939-40. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee for first degree murder and sentence of death. The jury unanimously found the presence of one statutory aggravating circumstance, that defendant had previously been convicted of a violent felony offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another individual were involved in the robbery and murder of a victim. Defendant told the individual in a phone call that defendant's girlfriend knew too much and had to go. After she and defendant were heard fighting, the girlfriend's body was found. The court held that because defendant had filed several pro se motions, he was capable of filing a waiver had he been adamant about representing himself. Also, denying counsel's motion to withdraw was not error because it would have caused further delay and there was no indication that counsel had any further adverse incident with defendant subsequent to one threat. The record supported the finding that defendant posed a substantial security risk for the courtroom and that the use of restraints was warranted. The evidence was sufficient that the murder was premeditated in that the victim was unarmed, it was indicated that she was asleep in her bed, and defendant had stated his intentions to get rid of her. Further, evidence of the first murder and burglary was properly introduced to show motive and premeditation, and the trial court properly instructed the jury on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Harwood


No. M2004-01811-CCA-R9-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 988


March 8, 2005, Session  
September 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Harwood, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 39 (Tenn., Jan. 30, 2006)
Affirmed by State v. Pickett, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 10 (Tenn., Jan. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Interlocutory Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2003-B-843. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) with four counts of sexual exploitation of a minor. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal to challenge the trial court's denial of his motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003 was unconstitutional because the term "possess" was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court of appeals disagreed. It was apparent that accidental possession of the prohibited materials was not enough to satisfy the State's burden of knowing possession. Indeed, one who received an unsolicited email or advertisement that contained child pornography had not overtly acted at all, much less knowingly. Similarly, one who accidentally opened a disguised email or inadvertently visited a web page containing child pornography could not be said to have acted with awareness that he or she was taking knowing possession of prohibited material. Although defendant claimed that citizens could "inadvertently, but knowingly possess prohibited images on their computers," that argument was oxymoronic and attempted to expand the scope of the statute beyond that which was established by the plain meaning of its terms.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Demonbreun v. Bell


No. M2005-00563-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 990



September 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Demonbreun v. Bell, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1190 (Tenn., Dec. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 94-B-1274. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge
Demonbreun v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 679 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a second pro se petition for habeas corpus relief, in which he contended that he was entitled to habeas corpus relief because he was deprived of the right to a jury trial and his indictment was insufficient. The Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) issued an order dismissing the petition, finding that, inter alia, petitioner failed to adhere to the mandatory requirements for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner failed to adhere to the mandatory requirements for habeas corpus petitions under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107. He falsely stated that the instant petition was his first petition for writ of habeas corpus on the instant case, when he had previously filed a habeas corpus petition in the same case and in the same court. Petitioner failed to attach his previous petition and the order denying it, and he failed to give satisfactory reasons for failing to comply with the mandates of § 29-21-107. Further, he alleged that his indictment was insufficient, but he failed to attach his indictment to his petition for the trial court's review. However, even if petitioner had complied with the statutory requirements, he would not be entitled to relief. Petitioner's first claim was that his sentence for his conviction for conspiracy to sell over 300 grams of cocaine was unconstitutional in light of Blakely v. Washington. Petitioner's claim regarding his sentence based on Blakely was not a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner failed to establish by a preponderance of the evidence that his conviction was void or his term of imprisonment had expired.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Ralph


No. M2004-02293-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 925


April 12, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
August 25, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Ralph, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 62 (Tenn., Feb. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3, Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Warren County. No. F-8552. Larry B. Stanley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Circuit Court for Warren County (Tennessee) found defendant guilty of failure to display a driver's license; resisting arrest; and simple possession of a Schedule III controlled substance. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms for an effective sentence of 11 months and 29 days. The trial court suspended all but 120 days of defendant's effective sentence, and placed defendant on probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: It was necessary to show a police officer both the front and the back of the driver's license in order to comply with the display requirements set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-50-351(a). Because defendant did not allow the officer to look at the back of his license, he failed to comply with § 55-50-351(a). Thus, defendant was lawfully arrested for failure to display his driver's license. Accordingly, the drugs found in defendant's vehicle were discovered during a lawful search incident to his arrest. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the drugs found in his truck during a search incident to his arrest. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction for resisting arrest, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-602, because (1) after defendant refused to show the officer his license, the officer asked defendant to exit his vehicle, but he refused; (2) the officer called for back up, but he still refused exit his vehicle; (3) the officer then placed him under arrest; (4) the officer had to forcibly pull him from the vehicle; and (5) defendant continued to struggle on the ground as the officers attempted to handcuff him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Circuit Court for Blount County. No. C-11100. D. Kelly Thomas, Jr.

DISPOSITION: Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Blount County (Tennessee), which convicted defendant of first degree premeditated murder with one aggravating circumstance. Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: A boyfriend offered money to kill the victim, who allegedly raped his girlfriend. Defendant, the boyfriend, and others went to the victim's residence and shot him. The court held among other things: (1) a jury could infer that after proclaiming he needed the reward money and obtaining a gun, defendant went to the victim's house and shot him; (2) although defendant was tried by a Caucasian jury, he failed to show that if the representation of African Americans was underrepresented in the petit jury, it was the result of systematic exclusion; (3) the decision to admit an excited utterance during testimony could not be impugned by testimony of the hearsay declarant that was not presented until later; (4) the trial court erred in failing to require defense counsel to conduct an inquiry into defendant's right to testify under the Momon guidelines; (5) the circumstances included none of the exacerbating indicia that justified the death penalty in other gunshot-inflicted homicides as the application of the Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(2) (2003) factor was based upon a single prior conviction, aggravated robbery and defendant's role in the homicide, though major, may have been vicarious.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence of death. The court also remanded for a new sentencing hearing should the trial court determine that Momon error was not committed or was harmless.

State v. Presnell


No. E2004-00266-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 880


March 22, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
August 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation February 21, 2006.
Appeal denied by State v. Presnell, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 135 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Cocke County. No. 6413. Rex Henry Ogle, Judge.
State v. Presnell, 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 784 (Tenn., Nov. 5, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Cocke County (Tennessee) of aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was denied his right to a speedy trial. The court of appeals disagreed. Although there was a delay of almost 8 years, many of the delays were caused by defendant or at the least acquiesced to by defendant. There was no evidence that the State was delaying prosecution of defendant to gain a tactical advantage or to harass him. The delays did not occur because of bureaucratic indifference. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal which also delayed his trial. Defendant was aware of the charges against him and he did not mitigate the effect of the delay in his failure to raise the issue earlier in the proceedings. The trial court found that there was no prejudice to defendant since he could have taken the deposition of a few of the witnesses in question. In addition, defendant did not subpoena another witness, and the trial court questioned the witness's unavailability.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hooper


No. E2004-01053-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 864


February 8, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
August 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hooper, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1164 (Tenn., Dec. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 242458. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) of rape and incest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court's error in not allowing him to cross-examine the victim concerning the information contained within the Children's Advocacy Center report was not harmless. The court of appeals disagreed. Although the trial court's erroneous ruling under Tenn. R. Evid. 412 prevented defendant from asking the victim whether she made a false allegation of rape and from questioning her regarding some of the circumstances surrounding that event, the error was harmless. The rule against hearsay would have prevented defendant from asking the victim about the alleged rapist's daughter's statement. Because the victim testified at the proffer that she did not make a false allegation of rape, Tenn. R. Evid. 608 would have operated to prevent defendant from calling the alleged rapist or his daughter to contradict the victim's denial. In addition, defendant failed to show the necessary prejudice to establish a due process violation for the State's delayed disclosure of the Children's Advocacy Center report.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Booker v. Carlton


No. E2005-00231-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 790



August 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Booker v. State, 2017 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 683 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 7, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Johnson County. No. 4507. Robert E. Cupp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Johnson County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition for writ of habeas corpus. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the trial court's denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to aggravated robbery. He was sentenced according to the terms of his plea agreement. He filed for habeas relief. The petitioner's claims of an involuntary guilty plea, ineffective assistance of counsel, and the States's failure to provide notice of its intent to seek an enhanced sentence, were not cognizable claims for habeas corpus relief. These claims, even if proven, would not render the judgment void. Petitioner's argument on appeal that Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-101 et seq. was unconstitutional was waived because he failed to present it in his habeas corpus petition. The petitioner failed to establish that he was entitled to habeas corpus relief.

Davis v. State


No. E2004-01394-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 704


March 22, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
July 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Davis v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1181 (Tenn., Dec. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 71411. Ray L. Jenkins, Judge.
State v. Davis, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 244 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 15, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee), dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief, in which he alleged, inter alia, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel at trial. Petitioner had been convicted of especially aggravated kidnapping, aggravated robbery, misdemeanor theft, and two counts of aggravated rape.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, petitioner argued that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to adequately investigate the facts and prepare for trial, failing to effectively raise the defense of consent, and denying him the opportunity to testify on his own behalf at trial by telling him that he would be "stupid" if he chose to testify. The appellate court held that petitioner was afforded the effective assistance of counsel. Petitioner conceded in his brief that, given the largely unrebutted testimony provided at the post-conviction hearing regarding counsel's fact investigation, it could not honestly be argued that those activities amounted to ineffective representation. Additionally, the transcript of the trial revealed that trial counsel raised the issue of consent on at least two occasions. Finally, trial counsel admitted to the statement regarding petitioner's testimony but stated that she left the ultimate decision about the testimony to petitioner, and petitioner admitted on cross-examination that he had the ultimate choice on whether he would testify and that he voluntarily chose not to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

678 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Deakins v. State


No. E2004-01803-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 682


February 8, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
July 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Deakins v. Westbrooks, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 775 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 245236. Steven M. Bevil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor, sexual exploitation of a minor, and statutory rape. The trial court denied post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel because his trial attorneys did not challenge the constitutionality of the Tennessee Protection of Children Against Sexual Exploitation Act (PCSEA), Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-17-1001 to 1007. The appellate court found that it did not need to reach the question of the constitutionality of the PCSEA. From the testimony at the post-conviction hearing, it was evident that defendant was well aware of the constitutional issues surrounding his case. Defendant testified that he accepted the State's third plea offer because he wanted to get out of jail. Defendant was well aware of the issues surrounding the constitutionality of the PCSEA and made a conscious decision to accept the State's offer. He failed to show that his attorneys' performance was deficient or that he was prejudiced by any deficiency.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
