Myers v. State


No. M2004-02411-CCA-MR3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 676


April 5, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
June 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for White County. No. CR 899 Lillie Ann Sells, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for White County (Tennessee) denying his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction of one count of attempted rape upon entry of a best-interest guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to the attempted rape of his girlfriend's daughter, and was sentenced to six years in prison. On appeal of the district court's judgment denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, the court held that several issues defendant raised were not properly before the court because he failed to cite to the record or to authorities, as required by Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 10(b) and Tenn. R. App. P. 27(a)(7). The following issues were not subject to post-conviction relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-103: (1) that the available evidence would prove defendant's factual and actual innocence; (2) that he was subjected to an unlawful arrest; (3) that defendant was not given immediate access to evidence; and (4) that he was denied the effective assistance of post-conviction counsel. Defendant waived his claim that he was denied due process because of an unconstitutional and illegal conspiracy by the prosecution, the judge, and both defense attorneys to convict, sentence, and imprison him because he failed to raise the claim in his post-conviction petition. Defendant also waived three claims by failing to provide a complete record.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

 

680 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hayes


No. M2004-00715-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


190 S.W.3d 665; 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 645


February 16, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
June 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 97-C-1735. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, revoked defendant's probation after it was alleged that defendant violated probation by possessing cocaine. The trial court found that the police search was valid and revoked defendant's suspended sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the cocaine was illegally seized and the evidence should have been suppressed. The appellate court noted that the record was void of any evidence of reasonable suspicion of criminal activity, such that defendant's detention constituted a de facto arrest. The search and seizure of the cocaine was unreasonable as no Miranda warnings were provided to defendant, consent immediately followed the illegal seizure, and no intervening event occurred. However, exclusion of evidence in a revocation hearing that was obtained as a result of police harassment or obtained in a particularly offensive manner was consistent with Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-311(d) which permitted the trial judge to enter judgment as the trial judge may deem right and proper under the evidence presented. The officer was not informed that defendant was a probationer, only that he had prior convictions. In the absence of any evidence of police harassment or that the evidence was obtained in a particularly offensive manner, the exclusionary rule was not applicable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

681 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Henderson v. State


No. W2003-01545-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 667



June 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Henderson v. Bell, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 40333 (W.D. Tenn., June 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Fayette County. No. 4465. Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.
State v. Henderson, 24 S.W.3d 307, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 390 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court for Fayette County (Tennessee) to first degree premeditated murder, especially aggravated kidnapping, aggravated robbery, attempted especially aggravated kidnapping, aggravated assault, and felonious escape. The trial court imposed the death sentence and denied postconviction relief. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that the postconviction court erred by failing to recuse itself because it demonstrated bias by its attitude and behavior regarding a defense expert witness. The court of appeals disagreed. At the conclusion of the expert's testimony, the postconviction court questioned the expert about his motives for changing careers from teaching at a university to becoming a mitigation specialist and sentencing consultant. The petitioner argued that, by questioning the witness at length, taking notes during his testimony and "smiling" at the prosecutor during the testimony, the postconviction judge created the appearance that he was taking sides. However, the judge presided over the postconviction hearing, without a jury, and while expressing those sentiments before a jury might have given rise to concern that the trial judge's statements or actions prejudiced the finder of fact, that concern was not present where the trial judge was the trier of fact. Therefore, it was not error for the postconviction judge to fail to recuse himself for questioning the expert.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

682 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. Bell


No. M2004-02667-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 653


April 5, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
June 27, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. Tenn. R. App. P. 3. Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. No. 3568. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, to second-degree murder and was sentenced to 25 years in prison. Thereafter, he filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, which the trial court summarily denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was a minor at the time of the offense. He contended that the juvenile court was required by law to find reasonable grounds at a transfer hearing before transferring him to criminal court. Defendant asserted that the only finding in the transfer order was the judge's notation "Waived by the Defendant." He further argued that his sentence was illegal because the trial court applied enhancement factors based upon facts not found by a jury or admitted by him. The appellate court held that transfer order was properly signed and dated; therefore, the trial court had authority and jurisdiction to convict and sentence defendant. The appellate court further held that the claimed defect, even if true, did not constitute a jurisdictional defect; thus, defendant presented a voidable claim, which was not cognizable in a petition for writ of habeas corpus. The appellate court concluded that defendant's reliance on Blakely and his accompanying argument failed in many respects, and that where the allegations in a petition for writ of habeas corpus did not demonstrate that the judgment was void, a trial court could correctly dismiss the petition without a hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Clifton v. State


No. W2004-01385-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 582


October 5, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
June 9, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County No. 04-CR-8562. R. Lee Moore, Jr., Judge.
State v. Clifton, 1984 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 2850 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 31, 1984)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who was serving a life sentence as a habitual offender, appealed a judgment of the Lake County Circuit Court, Tennessee, which dismissed his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he was improperly classified as a habitual offender because he lacked the requisite number of necessary felony convictions, that his underlying convictions included illegally-imposed concurrent sentences, and that the habeas corpus court improperly refused to appoint counsel in his case or hold an evidentiary hearing on the issues raised in his petition. With respect to the propriety of the inmate's habitual offender classification, the instant court concluded that the law of the case doctrine barred its reconsideration of the issue. With respect to the legality of the underlying convictions supporting the inmate's habitual offender classification, the instant court concluded that the inmate could not use the writ of habeas corpus to attack his predicate convictions because the sentences on those convictions had been served and had expired. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-101 (2000), for the inmate to be eligible for habeas corpus relief, it was necessary that he be imprisoned or restrained of liberty. The inmate could not attack these convictions because he was no longer imprisoned or restrained of his liberty in consequence of them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Friedman


No. M2004-01266-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 574


May 10, 2005, Session  
June 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Friedman, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 11 (Tenn., Jan. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Giles County. No. 10968. Stella L. Hargrove, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Giles County, Tennessee, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of promoting prostitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37, defendant reserved as a certified question of law the issue of whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-512 (2003), et seq., under which he was indicted, was unconstitutional. The appellate court noted that the record evinced that the requirements of Rule 37 were met. There was no dispute that the challenged statutory provision did not involve a suspect class, thus, the appellate court's initial determination remained whether defendant's right to own and operate a business where he was aware that his employees engaged in sexual activity with his customers for a monetary fee was a guaranteed "fundamental right." Prostitution was not constitutionally protected conduct. Consenting adults had a right to privacy that extended to entitled them, in certain circumstances, to engage in sexual activity in the privacy of their home, there was no such entitlement to do so in a public place. Therefore, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-512 did not infringe on defendant's fundamental right of privacy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Reid

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 556


November 17, 2004, Session  
June 3, 2005, Filed

State v. Reid, 164 S.W.3d 286, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 481 (Tenn., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of three counts of premeditated murder, three counts of felony murder, one count of attempted murder, and one count of especially aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting a videotape of the crime scene because it was not necessary to establish the position of the bodies or the description of the crime scene. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court found that the video was relevant to show the position of the victims, to give an accurate description of the crime scene, to corroborate testimony, to show the location of the victims' hats, to show the location of the shell casings, and to show intent. The trial court further found that the probative value of the videotape was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice. The crime scene video of most homicides necessarily depicted the bodies of the victims as they were found and the blood of the victims. If the court of appeals were to accept defendant's argument in that regard, no crime scene videotapes of murders would ever be admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Huskey


No. E2002-02317-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


177 S.W.3d 868; 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 543


July 22, 2003, Session  
June 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Huskey, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 987 (Tenn., Oct. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 51903. Richard R. Baumgartner, Judge.
State v. Huskey, 82 S.W.3d 297, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 265 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) with four counts of murder. The State appealed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court properly suppressed his statements because the investigating officers did not "scrupulously honor" his invocation of his right to remain silent. The court of appeals agreed. Despite two invocations of the right to counsel, investigators continued to approach defendant and either interrogate him directly or attempt to endear themselves to him in hopes that he would discuss the investigations. The record reflected that an officer spoke to a jailmate of defendant and asked whether defendant discussed with him about what the detectives had talked to defendant on November 4 and 5. It was simply unreasonable to conclude that the officer was not referring to substantive conversations he and the other detectives had with defendant on November 4 and 5. Therefore, after the defendant invoked his right to remain silent, the detectives re-questioned him at least three additional times and met with him on two other occasions where, at the least, the conversations concerned the same subject matter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

King v. State


No. M2004-01371-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 548


April 5, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
June 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by King v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 720 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 19, 2005)
Appeal denied by King v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1192 (Tenn., Dec. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County Nos. 39051 and 41153. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.
State v. King, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 673 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 1, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) convicted petitioner inmate, upon his guilty plea, of one count of selling over .5 grams of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school, a Class A felony. He agreed to be sentenced as a Range I offender to 15 years. The inmate subsequently filed for post-conviction relief raising challenges to his indictment, conviction, and sentence. After a hearing, the trial court denied relief. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the inmate was not entitled to relief on the basis of his allegations concerning the post-conviction trial judge. Also, the inmate claimed that his sentence was illegal because it was outside the Range I sentence for a Class B felony. However, the inmate pled guilty to selling over .5 grams of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school. The sale of over .5 grams of cocaine was normally a Class B felony, but, because the sale was made within 1,000 feet of a school, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-432(b), the inmate's offense was punishable by one classification higher than was provided in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417(b)-(i). Accordingly, the inmate was subject to being sentenced for a Class A felony. The inmate knew that he was pleading guilty to a Class A felony at his guilty plea hearing. The Range I sentence for a Class A felony was 15 to 25 years. Thus, the inmate's 15-year sentence was not illegal. Additionally, the appellate court found that because Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-432 did not create an offense, it could not contain any lesser offenses. Thus, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417 was not a lesser-included offense of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-432.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Madison County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of aggravated burglary and rape. He was sentenced to concurrent sentences of fifteen years for aggravated burglary and sixteen years for rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence presented at trial was insufficient to support the verdict, that the trial court erred in admitting DNA evidence, and that his sentence was improper. The appellate court noted that defendant intelligently and voluntarily consented to a search, even though he was aware of his right to refuse. In light of the substantial interests of the State, the diminished privacy interests of convicted felons, and the minimal intrusion caused by the taking of blood samples, the collection and maintenance of DNA samples pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-321, was reasonable. The evidence was sufficient to support the finding that defendant was the person who committed the crimes where the DNA profile from the victim's rape kit matched defendant's DNA profile and an expert witness concluded that no other person could have been the source of the semen. The trial court properly gave great weight to defendant's previous history of criminal convictions, and properly considered the enhancement factor that defendant had a previous history of unwillingness to comply with the conditions of his release.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kincer


No. M2004-01403-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Van Buren County, Tennessee, found defendant guilty of facilitation of the manufacture of one hundred grams or more of a substance containing methamphetamine. The trial court sentenced the defendant to four years. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police executed a search warrant and discovered numerous items at the residence that were associated with the manufacture of methamphetamine. The investigator removed a bottle of heat gas treatment, a glass bowl with a funnel and red phosphorous residue, and two jars with multi-layered liquids, one of which tested positive for the presence of methamphetamine, from defendant's truck. Defendant's claim that the facilitation statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-403, was vague was not preserved for review.

State v. Green


No. M2003-02774-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 432


December 7, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
May 5, 2005, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of three counts of aggravated robbery and three counts of robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the robbery conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. During the robbery, the victim recognized defendant as the same person who robbed her a few days earlier--the same person she testified she believed had a gun the first time they met. During the first robbery, she feared that defendant would rape or kill her. The victim quickly complied with all of defendant's orders during the second robbery, including opening the safe and giving him the security system video tape. When the police called and told her to leave the phone off the hook she did not, testifying that she "couldn't" because she was afraid defendant would become suspicious. When defendant forced her into the restroom she remained inside until she was informed the police had defendant in custody. That evidence supported the jury's conclusion that the victim was in fear during the second robbery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were modified. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Kirkham v. State


No. M2004-02635-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 422


March 9, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
May 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Kirkham v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 872 (Tenn., Oct. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sumner County. No. 820-1999. Jane Wheatcraft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the judgment of the Criminal Court for Sumner County, Tennessee, dismissing his habeas corpus petition.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner alleged fatal deficiencies in the indictment, an involuntary, unintelligent and unknowing guilty plea, an illegal and void sentence, and ineffective assistance of counsel. Upon review, the appellate court ruled that the petitioner had not presented any claims that justified habeas corpus relief. The challenges to the validity of a guilty plea rendered the conviction voidable, not void; therefore, they were not cognizable in a habeas corpus petition but were appropriately addressed in a petition for postconviction relief. Also, the petitioner's sentence was not facially void. The petitioner pled guilty to robbery, a class C felony, and received a sentence of eight years, which was certainly within the appropriate range. Furthermore, the petitioner was sufficiently notified of the charges against him, and the trial court had authority to enter the judgment following his plea. The petitioner was properly named, the date of the offense was given, the statute relied upon was recited, the statutory language was tracked, and the elements relied upon were listed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ely v. Deroyal Indus.


No. E2004-00865-WC-R3-CV


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 414

694 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Earls v. State


No. M2003-03011-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 364


January 26, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
April 19, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marshall County. No. 14185. Lee Russell, Judge.
State v. Earls, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 593 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 18, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of four counts of forgery, Class E felonies, and one count of theft under $ 500, a Class A misdemeanor. He was sentenced as a career offender to an effective sentence of twelve years. After a hearing, the Circuit Court for Marshall County, Tennessee, denied him post-conviction relief. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the hearing on defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, his trial lawyer testified that he prepared a motion for new trial. However, he acknowledged that he did not file it within the thirty-day time limit set forth in Tenn. R. Crim. App. 33(b). The appellate court held that defendant suffered from the ineffective assistance of counsel due to his lawyers failure to timely file the motion; there was a presumption of prejudice. Therefore, defendant was entitled to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling was reversed, and the matter was remanded with instructions to the trial court that it grant the defendant a delayed appeal, beginning with the right to file a delayed motion for a new trial.

Conn v. State


No. M2004-00220-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 370


February 8, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
April 19, 2005, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Case Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-A-389. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denying his pro se petition for post-conviction relief without the appointment of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted of possession with intent to sell twenty-six grams or more of a schedule II controlled substance, felony possession of a weapon, possession of drug paraphernalia, and possession of a controlled substance. He filed a pro se fill-in-the-blank "Petition for Relief from Conviction or Sentence" and "Uniform Civil Affidavit of Indigency." The post-conviction court, by order, found that the petitioner had failed to state sufficient grounds for his constitutional claims and dismissed his petition when he failed to amend it within fifteen days. On review, the appellate court held that he should have been appointed counsel pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(e). The claims presented in his original pro se petition, along with his subsequent request for counsel, entitled him to the appointment of counsel to aid him in drafting a more complete petition.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the petitioner's post-conviction petition was reversed, and the case was remanded for appointment of counsel.

State v. Shields


No. M2004-03056-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 358



April 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Motion denied by Shields v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 885 (Tenn., Oct. 17, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Shields v. Tennessee, 546 U.S. 1219, 126 S. Ct. 1442, 164 L. Ed. 2d 141, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1913 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Shields v. Bell, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 903 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County No. 50553. Don R. Ash, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had previously pled guilty in the Circuit Court for Rutherford County, Tennessee, to the offense of rape and received a 10-year prison sentence. Thereafter, he filed petition for a writ of habeas corpus primarily challenging the constitutionality of the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989 in light of Blakely. The trial court denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his petition, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989 in light of Blakely, and argued that because the enhancement factors used to increase his sentence were not included in the indictment, his indictment failed to allege the necessary facts to constitute the offense with which he was charged. The appellate court initially noted that although defendant's pre se notice of appeal was not filed within the 30-day time period of Tenn. R. App. P. 4, it would waive the timely filing of the notice of appeal in the interest of justice to address the issues on the merits. The appellate court held that the state supreme court recently determined that Blakely did not announce a new rule of law and that the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989 did not authorize a sentencing procedure which violated the Sixth Amendment right to jury trial. The appellate court further held that while if the indictment charging defendant were fatally defective, the issue could have been raised in a habeas corpus petition; however, he failed to include his indictments with his petition; thus, he was not entitled to relief on the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Reynolds v. State

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 319

Reynolds v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 501 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 8, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, challenged the judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner pled guilty to two counts of aggravated rape and was sentenced to concurrent thirty-five year sentences, and the petitioner did not file a direct appeal. The petitioner had previously filed two petitions for writs of habeas corpus, both of which were denied. The petitioner claimed that the minimum sentence he could have received was twenty years, thus, when the trial court imposed sentences of thirty-five years after improperly applying enhancement factors that were not found by a jury or admitted by the petitioner, the trial court acted in contravention of the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision, rendering his sentences illegal. The appellate court ruled that the petitioner failed to demonstrate that his convictions or sentences were void. Also, Blakely did not establish a new watershed rule, and that Blakely did not apply retroactively to cases on collateral appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

698 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Butler


No. E2004-00359-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 302


October 27, 2004, Session  
March 30, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. Nos. 76909, 77455. Richard Baumgartner, Judge, and Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant one filed an interlocutory appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County, Tennessee, which denied his motion to dismiss a child pornography possession case under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003 and determined that only a portion of the statute was unconstitutional. The State appealed the orders in cases against defendant one and defendant two for the State to produce the alleged pornographic material.


OVERVIEW: Defendant two was charged under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1004. The trial court ordered the State under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 16(a)(1)(C) (2004) to copy evidence in defendant one's case, and provide a mirror image of defendant two's hard drive. The court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003(b), by allowing a jury to infer that a participant is a minor if the material represented or depicted the participant as a minor came too close to permitting a conviction when an actual minor was not involved. However, the rest of the statute, severed from subsection (b), did not proscribe the possession of "virtual" child pornography or material containing youthful-looking adults. As to the risk that someone who received an unsolicited email could be charged, the expert testified that it was possible to distinguish a file that had been accidentally placed on a hard drive. Therefore, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court further held that the copying of the pornographic materials did not violate the sexual exploitation of a minor statutes in the context of the prosecution or defendant of a case under the statute and the motions to compel were properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rulings of the trial courts.

State v. Hill

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Scott County (Tennessee) of nine counts of sexual battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant admitted that "on more than one occasion he was sexually stimulated" by the contact with the victim, even if it was for a medical purpose. Additionally, the victim testified that on one occasion when defendant was in the shower with the victim, he became partially erect. At trial, defendant defended upon grounds that the contact was not for sexual purposes; however, that argument was obviously rejected, as evidenced by the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Livingston


No. M2004-00086-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 247


October 13, 2004, Session  
March 15, 2005, Filed

Appeal granted by State v. Livingston, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 671 (Tenn., Aug. 22, 2005)
Reversed by State v. Livingston, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 641 (Tenn., July 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-B-625. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and sentence modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, convicted defendant on a jury verdict of evading arrest by motor vehicle with risk of death or injury. As a career offender, he was sentenced to twelve years. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The conviction challenged in this appeal stemmed from an automobile chase through the streets of central Nashville, Tennessee. On appeal, the court held that the evading arrest statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-603(b) was not an unconstitutional violation of the Caption Clause, Tenn. Const. II, § 7; there was sufficient evidence to sustain defendant's conviction; (3) there was sufficient proof of risk of injury or death to convict defendant of Class D felony evading arrest; the defendant was not denied his right to effective assistance of counsel because his trial counsel failed to request jury instructions on a lesser-included offense and failed to challenge the unlawfulness of the attempted arrest; and the defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a trial by jury was not violated when the trial court made findings of fact for "sentence enhancing purposes." However, the trial court erred in sentencing him as a career offender, because the State's notice of intent to seek enhanced punishment was defective.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment as to the Class D felony conviction was affirmed, but the defendant's sentence was modified to four years to be served in the Tennessee Department of Correction as a Range I standard offender.

State v. Stephenson


No. E2003-01091-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 208


November 16, 2004, Session  
March 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Stephenson, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 454 (Tenn., June 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Cocke County. No. 5012 & 5040. Ben W. Hooper, II, Judge.
Stephenson v. Carlton, 28 S.W.3d 910, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 534 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence of death in the Circuit Court for Cocke County (Tennessee) where he was convicted of first degree murder and conspiracy to commit first degree murder. On remand, there were resentencing proceedings at which the jury found as the sole aggravating circumstance that defendant committed the murder for remuneration or employer another to commit murder for remuneration under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of participating in the murder of his wife. The court affirmed and held: (1) aggravating circumstances need not be included as actual elements of the offense for purposes of conducting a comparison of statutory elements of the offenses; (2) conspiracy and murder were not the same offenses and Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-12-106(c) codified the legislature's intent that prosecution for conspiracy and the underlying offense was proper; (3) the Tennessee Supreme court had rejected the argument that aggravating circumstances must be charged in the indictment under the capital sentencing scheme in Tennessee; (4) the Confrontation Clause did not apply to sentencing proceedings and further defendant cross-examined the witnesses at trial; (5) at the sentencing hearing, defendant's guilt or innocence was not at issue and his rifle was admissible to show the nature of the crime; (6) when defendant questioned witnesses regarding the fact that he had no significant record, the State was entitled to offer proof in rebuttal; (7) the evidence supported the finding that the aggravating circumstance outweighed the mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Patrick


No. E2003-02382-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 225


October 26, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
March 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation September 12, 2005.
Appeal denied by State v. Patrick, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 766 (Tenn., Sept. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Blount County. Nos. C-13601, C-13602, C-13603. D. Kelley Thomas, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Blount County (Tennessee) convicted defendant of violating the Habitual Motor Vehicle Offenders Act, felony evading arrest with risk of death, and felony reckless endangerment. The trial court ordered him to serve the six-year sentences for violation of the Act and reckless endangerment concurrently. The trial court ordered that those sentences be served consecutively to the 12 year sentence for evading arrest. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant because (1) the first officer began to pursue a speeding vehicle, which sped up to an estimated speed of 100 miles per hour; (2) a second officer saw the driver briefly as he jumped out of the vehicle, but before the driver ran away from the vehicle; (3) the second officer recognized the individual as defendant; (4) the passenger said that defendant had been driving the car and that she had begged him to stop the car; and (5) a third officer, who was off duty and was sitting on his great aunt's porch about 20 feet from the vehicle, saw defendant jump out of the driver's side of the car. Also, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for Class D felony evading arrest as he was driving at an estimated speed of 100 miles an hour, there were other cars on the road, and there were several people outside and cars lining both sides of the street where he stopped. However, defendant's convictions for Class E felony reckless endangerment and Class D felony evading arrest violated his rights against double jeopardy. Therefore, the reckless endangerment conviction was merged into the conviction for felony evading arrest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Long


No. W2003-02522-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 199


October 5, 2004, Session  
March 4, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Henry County. No. 13480. Julian P. Guinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of one count of manufacturing methamphetamine and one count of possession of drug paraphernalia. The Circuit Court for Henry County (Tennessee) imposed a split sentence for the manufacturing conviction, with one year to be served and the remainder to be served on supervised probation, to run concurrently with a sentence of 11 months and 29 days for the possession charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the initial stop of his vehicle was invalid due to lack of probable cause and, even if valid, the subsequent search was illegal. The appellate court concluded that the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant's vehicle based on information that defendant had been observed buying large quantities of Sudafed or similar cold remedies, commonly known to be used in the manufacture of methamphetamine. In addition, the officer did not exceed the permissive scope of defendant's consent to look into his vehicle. Next, the appellate court found no merit in defendant's claim that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence three cans of starting fluid because the State failed to establish a proper chain of custody. Finally, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his manufacturing conviction. The appellate court agreed, noting that there was no proof that suggested that defendant was propagating any controlled substances. He did, however, have many of the precursors to manufacturing and thus, the State had a submissible case of attempted manufacturing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for manufacturing methamphetamine was reversed and dismissed, and the case was remanded for trial for attempted manufacturing of methamphetamine.

Smith v. State


No. M2004-00719-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 171


December 15, 2004, Session  
February 25, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Smith v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1022 (Tenn., Nov. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 96-A-155. Randall J. Wyatt, Judge.
State v. Smith, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1276 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 17, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that dismissed his request for post-conviction relief for failure to state a claim within the purview of the Post-Conviction Relief Act, which had not been waived or previously determined as provided in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(f) (2004). Petitioner was seeking relief from his conviction of premeditated first-degree murder and attempted first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought post-conviction relief alleging that evidence was obtained as the result of an illegal search; that the State failed to disclose exculpatory evidence; that he received ineffective assistance of counsel; that newly discovered evidence would exonerate him; and that the grand and petit juries were improperly selected. Petitioner's attorney had filed a motion for withdrawal based on difficulties representing petitioner. Before denying counsel's motion to withdraw, the lower court dismissed the petition, noting that each claim was either waived or had been previously determined. On review, the court held that the lower court properly dismissed the petition without an evidentiary hearing and that the delay in the disposition of the petition did not prejudice petitioner, thus, any error would have been harmless. The court held that the lower court was well within its authority to consider the petition prior to ruling on counsel's motion to withdraw. The court noted that the lower court did file its order more than 30 days after the filing of the amended petition as specified in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(a) but that § 40-30-106 was only directory and not mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that denied post-conviction relief.

State v. Young

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County Nos. 00-04017, 00-04018, 00-04019 Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of premeditated first degree murder, especially aggravated kidnapping, and theft of property over $ 1,000. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the murder conviction because it was insufficient to show premeditation. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence established that in order to avoid apprehension by police, defendant carjacked the victim in midtown Memphis. The victim died as a result of a stab wound to the back. The blade of the knife broke off in the victim's chest cavity. The victim had bruising about the face, neck, and right thigh, which occurred less than two hours prior to death.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hall


No. M2003-02326-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 87


September 21, 2004, Session  
February 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Hall, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 847 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2001-D-1974. Walter Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of second degree murder and facilitation of second degree murder, respectively. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: One defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his facilitation of second degree murder conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. Based on defendant's participation in the planning stage of the offense, his transportation of the other defendant to and from the scene, his knowledge that a firearm would be involved, and his initial presence at the apartment building prior to the shooting, a jury could conclude that defendant knew that the other defendant intended to knowingly shoot the victim, and that he knowingly furnished substantial assistance during the planning stage of the offense and up to the point of actual confrontation with the victim. Because defendant left the scene before the other defendant shot the victim, a reasonable jury could also conclude that defendant did not intend to promote, assist, or benefit from the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

707 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Matthews


No. M2003-01889-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 92


October 13, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
February 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Matthews, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 510 (Tenn., May 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Houston County. No. 4510. Robert E. Burch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Houston County (Tennessee) of first degree premeditated murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: It was undisputed that defendant killed the victim by intentionally stabbing her to death. However, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the premeditation element of first degree murder. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence revealed that defendant planned the murder in his bedroom several hours before executing his plan. Defendant carefully selected the time of the murder to correspond with when the victim was most likely to be asleep. Defendant went first to the kitchen, selected a knife, and then proceeded to the victim's bedroom to carry out his plan. Based on that evidence, viewed in a light most favorable to the State, a rational finder of fact could find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant killed the victim intentionally and with premeditation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Galbreath v. State


No. M2003-02807-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 43


August 10, 2004, Session  
January 19, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bedford County. No. 9562. Lee Russell, Judge.
State v. Galbreath, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 620 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 26, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Bedford County (Tennessee), which convicted him of obtaining a prescription drug by fraud and subsequently denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of obtaining a prescription drug by fraud and his post-conviction motion was denied. On appeal, the court reversed that denial, holding that his counsel was ineffective at trial and on appeal for failing to request a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of facilitation and for failing to appeal the jury instruction issue. Thus, the court reversed the dismissal of the petition, reversed the original conviction, and remanded for a new trial. It appeared that counsel was trying to prove that the inmate was merely a facilitator of the felony and that he lacked the intent requested to commit the crime with which he was charged. Yet counsel did not request that the trial court give the jury a facilitation instruction, or object to the instructions given. The court could find no reasonable explanation for counsel's failure to raise the issue on direct appeal. His sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment considering his prior criminal convictions and his historically unsuccessful attempts at parole, probation, and rehabilitation. Thus, the sentence was not "grossly disproportionate" to his offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief, reversed the original conviction, and remanded for a new trial.

 

709 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bowman


No. W2003-02389-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 38


August 4, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
January 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bowman, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 525 (Tenn., May 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-01525. Chris Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of identity theft with the intent to avoid a court appearance. Defendant was sentenced as a Range I standard offender to serve three years in the workhouse. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not instructing the jury as to any lesser included offenses of identity theft and that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. Defendant conceded that he used his father's identity, but argued that the record did not contain any proof that he intended to commit any unlawful activity. The appellate court found that there was proof that defendant signed his father's name on the citation, which specified a court date. Defendant's father testified that he received a letter from the city court, stating that he had failed to appear for a court date. The evidence supported the inference that defendant used his father's identity in order to avoid a court appearance. None of defendant's proposed lesser included offenses were lesser included offenses of identity theft. Misdemeanor theft, fraudulent use of a driver license, and criminal impersonation were not lesser included offenses of identity theft under the guidelines set forth in a prior case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hall v. State


No. W2003-00669-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 3


October 5, 2004, Session  
January 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hall v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 590 (Tenn., June 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C00-422. Roy B. Morgan, Judge.
State v. Hall, 8 S.W.3d 593, 1999 Tenn. LEXIS 585 (Tenn., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Madison County (Tennessee) that denied his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction for capital murder of his estranged wife. Petitioner claimed he received ineffective assistance of counsel during trial and the penalty phase, and that the heinous, atrocious or cruel aggravating circumstance under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(5) and the death penalty were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The jury found that petitioner's murder of his wife was especially heinous, atrocious and cruel. Petitioner had cut the phone lines before forcing his way into his wife's home, inflicted many injuries while his children pleaded for him to stop, and then dragged his wife outside where he strangled and drowned her in the pool. The court affirmed the dismissal of the petition for post-conviction relief. The court held that the record did not support petitioner's claims that his counsel failed to present a proper intoxication defense or mitigation defense during the penalty phase. The court found that defense counsel relied upon a theory that petitioner acted in an impulsive rather than a premeditated manner and attempted to convince the jury that he was distraught, depressed, and intoxicated when he went to his wife's home attempting a reconciliation. The court also found that evidence was elicited that showed petitioner had a habit of disconnecting phone lines without any resulting harm. The court rejected petitioner's constitutional challenges to the death penalty and the aggravating factor on the ground they had been previously determined, waived, or not supported with evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that dismissed petitioner's request for post-conviction relief from his capital murder conviction.

State v. Ivy


No. W2003-00786-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.

The jury found the presence of two aggravating circumstances, which were that defendant had previously been convicted of a violent felony offense and that the murder was committed to avoid prosecution. State v. Aaron


No. M2002-02288-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1123


January 6, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
December 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Aaron, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 455 (Tenn., May 2, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Aaron v. State, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 74 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Vacated in Part; Affirmed in Part; Sentence Modified. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 99-D-2360. Walter Kurtz, Judge.
State v. Aaron, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 596 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 8, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed ; Sentence Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor and false imprisonment in the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee. His convictions and sentences were affirmed on appeal. He filed a petition to rehear based on the United States Supreme Court's decision in Blakely v. Washington, and the trial court's consideration of enhancement factors at sentencing. The instant court granted review.


OVERVIEW: In light of Blakely, defendant argued that the trial court violated his right to trial by jury guaranteed to him by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment when it enhanced his sentence as to the aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor offense, at least in part, by finding facts not submitted to the jury and proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court noted that Blakely made it clear that a trial court could enhance a sentence based upon prior convictions. Thus, the trial court's application of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(2) for defendant's prior convictions was proper. However, the trial court also applied enhancement factors under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(8) and (16). Respectively, factors (8) and (16) provided that the offense involved a victim and was committed to gratify defendant's desire for pleasure or excitement, and defendant abused a position of public or private trust. The appellate court held the trial court's application of those factors violated Blakely. Consequently, the appellate court modified defendant's sentence for especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor from 11 years to nine years.


OUTCOME: The previous opinion of the instant court affirming defendant's sentence was vacated. Defendant's sentence for the conviction of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor was modified. The remainder of the instant court's previous opinion affirming defendant's convictions was affirmed.

State v. Turner


No. M2003-02064-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1061


September 22, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
December 1, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-C-1790. Carol Soloman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) convicted defendant of two counts of identify theft and sentenced him to concurrent sentences of three years, with service of one year in confinement. In addition, defendant was ordered to pay restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised several issues. The appellate court held that: (1) the trial court did not err by failing to suppress an in-court identification, as there was no State action in arranging the courtroom "confrontation" between the witness and defendant and defendant was permitted to cross-examine the witness; (2) the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions despite defendant's argument that the proof was insufficient to show beyond a reasonable doubt that he was the person who committed the crimes. The identification testimony of a witness was properly admitted into evidence and there was testimony from three other witnesses regarding a distinctive way defendant held a pen. The evidence, considered in the light most favorable to the State, was more than sufficient to support the convictions; (3) the trial court failed to impose a sentence in accordance with sentencing guidelines; and (4) as the record was silent regarding any finding of defendant's ability to pay the ordered restitution during his period of probation and this was a required finding, the trial court erred in determining the amount of restitution.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. However, the case was remanded to the trial court for determinations of the appropriate sentences and defendant's ability to pay the ordered restitution consistent with this opinion.

State v. Walters


No. M2003-03019-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1053


July 20, 2004, Session  
November 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 10, 2004.
Appeal denied by State v. Walters, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 264 (Tenn., Mar. 21, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Walters v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 60 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for White County. No. CR599. Lillie Ann Sells, Judge.
State v. Walters, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 850 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for White County (Tennessee) convicted defendant of two counts of rape of a child, a Class A felony, and two counts of aggravated sexual battery, a Class B felony, and sentenced him to concurrent sentences of 25 years for each rape conviction and 12 years for each aggravated sexual battery conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had sexual intercourse with his girlfriend's 12-year-old daughter. He claimed the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions, arguing the victim's testimony was not credible. However, credibility was determined by the jury. The evidence was sufficient. Because no evidence existed to show that he formed the intent to penetrate the victim only after he touched her, his separate convictions for a bathroom incident violated double jeopardy, and his aggravated sexual battery conviction merged into his rape of a child conviction. Rape of a child required unlawful sexual penetration. The victim testified defendant penetrated her vagina twice with his penis. As there was no evidence that defendant only attempted to penetrate the victim, the trial court was not required to instruct on attempted child rape. Because aggravated sexual battery, child abuse, and Class B misdemeanor assault were lesser included offenses of child rape, the trial court erred by failing to instruct on those lesser included offenses, which was harmless error. The trial court improperly applied enhancement factors under Blakely, so defendant's sentences were reduced.


OUTCOME: The rape of a child convictions were affirmed. The aggravated sexual battery convictions violated double jeopardy and merged into the convictions for rape of a child. The case was remanded for modifying the judgments to reflect that the aggravated sexual battery convictions merged into the rape of a child convictions. Each of defendant's sentences for rape of a child was modified from 25 to 23 years.

Herron v. State


No. W2004-02533-CCA-R28-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1181



November 22, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-15632.
Herron v. Raney, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1074 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 19, 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion in summarily denying petitioner's motion under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-117 to reopen his post-conviction application. Petitioner's reliance on Blakely failed because it was not one of the narrow class of watershed procedural rules implicating fundamental fairness and accuracy of the criminal proceeding. Because it related to the method in which the enhancements were found, not the enhancements themselves, the rule announced in Blakely was procedural. Retrospective application of the rule to cases on collateral review was not required.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Scarbrough


No. E2003-02850-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 871


May 18, 2004, Session  
October 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Scarbrough, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 131 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)
Affirmed by State v. Scarbrough, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 1044 (Tenn., Nov. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 62279B. Ray L. Jenkins, Judge.
State v. Scarbrough, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 512 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 11, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of, inter alia, aggravated burglary and felony. The burglary conviction was affirmed on direct appeal but the case was remanded for retrial on the felony murder count. Prior to his second trial, the trial court applied the law of the case doctrine to prevent defendant from contesting his conviction for aggravated burglary. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court's order impinged on his rights to a jury trial and to present evidence in his defense. The court of appeals agreed. Defendant's constitutional right to a jury trial would be violated by the trial court's order which prevented him from presenting proof which would question the burglary conviction. Thus, just as he could not be collaterally estopped, for constitutional reasons, from presenting proof as to the burglary conviction, he, likewise, could not be barred, by application of the law of the case, from doing so. Of course, evidence presented in that regard must meet the admissibility requirements of the Tennessee Rules of Evidence. Although defendant suggested in his appellate brief that Tennessee law might allow the trial court to instruct the jury as to the existence of the burglary judgment at the end of the trial, that possible procedure was not briefed by the parties and, therefore, was not before the court of appeals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

719 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davenport


No. M2003-02303-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 866


July 20, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
October 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lalon R. Davenport, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 140 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. 53941. James K. Clayton, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Circuit Court for Rutherford County, Tennessee, to violating the Tennessee Motor Vehicle Habitual Offender Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-601 (1998 & Supp. 2003), et seq. Defendant appealed, reserving as a certified question of law the issue of whether the three-year time period articulated in the Act barred prosecution for violating the Act after the time period expired.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that since the Act provided for a three-year time period that a defendant was prohibited from driving and, as such, a defendant could not be in violation of the Act when driving more than three years after the entry of a judgment declaring him a habitual offender. The State responded that, by the language of the statute, any person found to be a habitual offender who thereafter was convicted of operating a motor vehicle in Tennessee while the judgment or order of the court prohibiting such operation was in effect committed a class E felony. The appellate court held that the legislature's articulation of a three-year time period in the Act did not bar prosecution of a defendant, who was apprehended for driving in violation of an order declaring him an habitual offender, even though he was driving more than three years after the entry of the order declaring him an habitual offender. The appellate court concluded that a defendant could not, by merely failing to file a petition, circumvent the requirement that the trial court restore his driving privileges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Kelly v. Mills


No. W2004-01106-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 876



October 8, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5846. Joe H. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for habeas corpus relief on the ground that he failed to attach the judgment or record of the proceedings upon which the judgment was rendered. The State filed a motion requesting that the court affirm the trial court's denial of relief, pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the attachment of a photocopy of the judgment form to defendant's motion to reconsider the trial court's denial of his petition failed to cure the deficiency in his actual petition. In granting the State's motion, the court found that the inmate had failed to attach the applicable judgments of conviction that he claimed were void to his petition. The procedural provisions of the habeas corpus statutes, particularly Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107, were mandatory and had to be followed scrupulously. Moreover, even assuming that the attachment of the judgment form to the motion to reconsider perfected the procedural requirements of the petition, the court held that the inmate had still failed to establish grounds for which the writ would issue because he failed to establish that his sentence had expired or that his sentences were illegal. The question of whether the Tennessee Department of Correction was properly calculating the inmate's sentence could not be raised in a habeas corpus proceeding. To challenge such calculations, the inmate had to proceed under the Tennessee Uniform Administrative Procedures Act in chancery court.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Walters


No. M2003-03019-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 850


July 20, 2004, Argued

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, modified in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The White County Criminal Court, Tennessee, convicted defendant of two counts of rape of a child and two counts of aggravated sexual battery. He was sentenced to concurrent sentences of 25 years for each rape conviction and 12 years for each aggravated sexual battery conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant came into the bathroom on her 12th birthday, touched her breasts and genital area, and put his penis in her vagina. DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder and was given consecutive life sentences. Defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was dismissed and affirmed on appeal. Defendant filed a pro se motion to reopen his post-conviction petition and a supplemental request for DNA analysis. The Criminal Court for Washington County, Tennessee, dismissed the motion and denied defendant's request for DNA analysis. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred by summarily dismissing the petition without allowing him to amend the petition after appointment of counsel.
