723 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Davidson v. Bell


No. M2003-01128-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 819


August 11, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
September 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Davidson v. Bell, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 993 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 03-C760. Barbara N. Haynes, Judge.
State v. Davidson, 1987 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 2649 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 21, 1987)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a fourth pro se petition for writ of habeas corpus in the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, alleging that the statutes under which he received a life sentence were unconstitutional. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition without a hearing. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his petition, the inmate argued that the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1982 and the habitual criminal statute under which he was sentenced to life imprisonment were unconstitutional as applied to him, as they violated his right to equal protection. The appellate court initially noted that habeas corpus relief would only be granted when it appeared upon the face of the judgment or the record of the proceedings upon which the judgment was rendered that a trial court lacked jurisdiction or authority to sentence a defendant or that the sentence had expired. The appellate court held that the habitual criminal statute did not violate the due process or equal protection provisions of the state or federal constitutions, nor did its imposition result in cruel and unusual punishment. Moreover, the appellate court concluded that the fact that the habitual criminal statute allowed prosecutorial selectivity in its applications created no constitutional infringement; therefore, the trial court committed no error in summarily dismissing the inmate's petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

724 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


No. M2003-02063-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 801


June 9, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
September 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mitchell v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 154 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Entry of Corrected Judgments. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 95-B-1222. Seth Norman, Judge.
State v. Mitchell, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 772 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 30, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed and Remanded for Entry of Corrected Judgments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief that alleged ineffective assistance of counsel, prosecutorial misconduct, improper jury instructions, double jeopardy violations, and the sentence. The inmate was convicted of two counts of rape, one count of attempted rape, and he pled nolo contendere a reduction to sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: The inmate signed and dated his original petition more than two months after the expiration of the one-year period of the date of the appellate decision and so consideration was barred under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a) (2003), but the court addressed the issues raised. The inmate alleged that counsel failed to subpoena the rape victim's alleged boyfriend as a witness to rebut the false testimony given in the presence of the jury by the alleged rape victim. The court held that because the witness was not produced at the evidentiary hearing, the inmate failed to show that he was prejudiced by counsel's not producing the witness at trial. As to the inmate's claim that Brady materials were not produced by the State, the inmate failed to explain in his petition or at the post-conviction hearing why the issue was not raised on direct appeal as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(g) (2003). Also, the Department of Corrections had no discretion regarding the inmate's sentence applying Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-523(b) and so did not err by classifying the inmate as a "multiple rapist." The court held that other claims were waived because they were not raised at the evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

725 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Banks


No. W2000-00963-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 793


October 7, 2003, Session  
September 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application denied by State v. Banks, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 65 (Tenn., Jan. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 96-06381-88. Joseph B. Brown, Jr., Judge.
State v. Banks, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 681 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of first-degree felony murder, first-degree premeditated murder, conspiracies to commit both modes of first-degree murder, especially aggravated burglary, especially aggravated robbery, three counts of especially aggravated kidnapping, and three counts of aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress his inculpatory statement. The court of appeals disagreed. The record supported the denial of the motion to suppress. An officer detailed an orderly process in which the officers advised defendant of his Miranda rights, procured a written waiver of his rights, obtained an informal statement, and procured defendant's adoption of a formal transcript of the statement. The officer's testimony that defendant waived his Miranda rights was not factually challenged. Thus, the State carried its burden of demonstrating that the high-school-educated defendant voluntarily and understandingly waived his rights. Furthermore, the officer affirmatively contradicted defendant's claim that his will to remain silent had been overborne by promises of leniency, physical discomfort, and threats that defendant's sister would lose her job unless the defendant confessed, and defendant's left hand was not handcuffed during the interview.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for conspiracy to commit first-degree felony murder was reversed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

726 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bellamy


No. E2004-00241-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 748



September 1, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sullivan County. No. S41,191, S41, 278 & S41, 485. R. Jerry Beck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee) imposed on petitioner inmate an effective term of 12 years' imprisonment, including two, concurrent six-year sentences and a third, consecutive, six-year sentence for the convictions of driving in violation of the motor vehicle habitual offender order. The inmate filed a motion to correct the illegal sentence. The trial court denied the inmate's motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted pursuant to guilty pleas of three counts of violating the Tennessee Motor Vehicle Habitual Offenders Act. The inmate filed a motion to vacate or to correct his allegedly illegal sentences. The inmate asserted that the sentences imposed upon his convictions for driving in violation of the motor vehicle habitual offenders act were illegal, because the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutionally void for vagueness. In particular, the inmate asserted that Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-616 failed to specify the punishment to be imposed for its violation. The trial court denied the motion, finding that the habitual traffic offender statutes were constitutional and legally correct. In the present case, the judgments reflected that, consistent with the applicable sentencing statutes, the inmate was sentenced as a career offender to a maximum Range III sentence of six years in prison for each conviction of driving in violation of a motor vehicle habitual offender order. Upon due consideration of the record, pleadings, and applicable law, the appellate court concluded that the trial court properly denied the inmate's motion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

727 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Page


No. W2003-01342-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 753


June 2, 2004, Session  
August 26, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Page, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 13 (Tenn., Jan. 18, 2005)
Reversed by State v. Page, 184 S.W.3d 223, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 37 (Tenn., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed; Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 99-09509. W. Fred Axley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court reversed; matter remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), after he was convicted by a jury of second degree murder. Defendant was subsequently sentenced as a Range II offender to 38 years in the Tennessee Department of Correction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an incident where he beat the victim to death as part of a group of four men. The appellate court generally held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction, as defendant hit the victim in the head repeatedly with a "plank" while others were doing likewise, such conduct was reasonably certain to cause death, and defendant was aware of his own actions. However, the trial court committed reversible error in failing to charge the jury on the lesser-included offense of facilitation of second degree murder, as defendant's failure to request the instruction did not waive his right to have the jury so instructed, and evidence existed that reasonable minds could accept as to facilitation of second degree murder because there was no proof establishing which of the four men struck the fatal blow(s). Additionally, the waiver provision of Tenn. Const. Ann. § 40-18-110(c) was constitutionally infirm as violative of a criminal defendant's fundamental constitutional right to have the jury charged on all lesser-included offenses embraced by the indictment and supported by the proof adduced at trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter to the trial court for a new trial. If further appellate review upheld defendant's conviction, the matter had to nonetheless be remanded for a determination of whether defendant personally waived his right to testify and, if not, whether that error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

730 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ramey


No. E2003-01840-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 636


March 16, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
July 15, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S46,096 R. Jerry Beck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee) that convicted him of the lesser-included offense of aggravated sexual battery under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-504 (2004) and imposed an 10-year prison sentence. Defendant claimed the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction, his sentence was excessive, and that an instruction as to the lesser-included offense of child abuse should have been given.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because there was no evidence of a specific incident or testimony as to the date of any particular offense. The court held that in cases where a defendant committed multiple offenses against the victim, the election doctrine only required the State to select which of multiple offenses in evidence it relied upon to seek the conviction. The court found that the State told the jury during closing arguments that it was electing a specific incident, that the victim testified about the particular details of that incident, and that references to other incidents were in very general terms, thus the jury must have relied on the specific incident in reaching its verdict. The court also held that the mid-range sentence imposed was clearly justified despite the trial court's failure to consider defendant's favorable sex offender evaluation for sentencing mitigation because the weight given to each enhancement or mitigating factor was within the discretion of the trial court. The court concluded that the failure to instruct the jury on the offense of child abuse was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant for aggravated sexual battery.

 

731 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hines v. State


No. M2004-01610-CCA-RM-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 630


June 28, 2004, Remanded By Supreme Court  
July 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hines v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 1048 (Tenn., Nov. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Cheatham County. No. 9852. Robert E. Burch, Judge.
Hines v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 618 (Tenn., June 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, convicted of first-degree felony murder and sentenced to death in the Circuit Court for Cheatham County, Tennessee, sought post-conviction relief. When the instant court denied relief, petitioner sought permission to appeal. The Tennessee Supreme Court granted the application and remanded.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court directed that on remand the instant court reconsider its previous conclusion that the trial court charged the incorrect version of the aggravating circumstance in Tenn. Code. Ann. § 39-2-203(i)(5) (1982). Inter alia, the court held that the trial court utilized the correct version of this statute when instructing the jury at the resentencing hearing as to aggravating circumstances. Trial counsel acknowledged that he knew a person, whom petitioner claimed committed the murder, was at the motel to rent a room with his paramour, but did not cross-examine him on this fact, as the sheriff did not want that person to be embarrassed and had assured trial counsel that the person knew nothing about the murder. Petitioner claimed that this was an actual conflict of interest and thus, there was a presumption of prejudice. The instant court held that trial counsel's failure to question the person regarding why he was at the motel did not result in counsel representing the sheriff's interests so there was no actual conflict. Moreover, petitioner would not have created residual doubt by arguing that the person he sought to have questioned had killed the victim.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the order of the post-conviction court denying the petition for post-conviction relief.

State v. Rice


No. W2002-00471-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 661


February 10, 2004, Session  
July 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation February 22, 2006..
Affirmed by State v. Rice, 184 S.W.3d 646, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 125 (Tenn., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-00035. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), after a jury found him guilty of first degree premeditated murder and of first degree felony murder. The trial court merged the convictions into one count of first degree murder. Following a sentencing hearing, the jury sentenced defendant to death, and the trial court approved of the sentencing verdict.


OVERVIEW: The case involved the murder and rape of a 13-year-old girl, defendant's stepdaughter. Defendant raised numerous issues on appeal. The appellate court generally held that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction, as defendant took police into the woods and led them to the location where the victim's body was found, and he was able to re-enact how the murder took place and able to describe how the victim was stabbed; (2) the trial court's improper restriction on defendant's cross-examination of a witness was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the witness was not the only witness testifying to the incriminating facts against defendant, and most of his testimony was corroborated by other witnesses; (3) there were no jury instruction errors; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by ordering defendant to sit in the front row behind defense counsel's table; and (5) defendant's sentence of death was not disproportionate considering the circumstances of the crime and defendant, as the case, taken as a whole, was not plainly lacking in circumstances consistent with other similar cases in which the death penalty had been imposed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and the sentence of death imposed by the trial court.

State v. Rogers


No. M2002-01798-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 574


January 13, 2004, Session  
June 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Rogers, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1080 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 27, 2004)
Application denied by State v. Rogers, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 67 (Tenn., Jan. 24, 2005)
Affirmed by State v. Rogers, 188 S.W.3d 593, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 123 (Tenn., 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Rogers v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 681 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 38939. Robert W. Wedemeyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first degree premeditated murder, especially aggravated kidnapping, rape of a child, and two counts of criminal impersonation. The jury found that the proof supported four aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(1), (2), (6), and (7) and sentenced defendant to death for the murder.


OVERVIEW: Five days before the victim's disappearance, defendant introduced himself to the nine-year-old victim as a police officer and offered to take her swimming and to shoot fireworks. Defendant returned to the victim's residence shortly before her disappearance. He admitted that she entered his car but claimed hat he accidentally backed over her and that he took her body and threw it over a bridge. The victim's remains were found months later in the woods. Her T-shirt was found inside-out nearby, and her shorts had semen stains on them. Defendant's wife testified that when he returned home the day of the victim's disappearance, blood was on his shirt, his pants and the car were muddy, and a child's fingerprints could be seen on the passenger side of the car's windshield. The court held that there was sufficient evidence from which a rational jury could have concluded that defendant kidnapped the victim near her home, drove her to a remote area, and killed her with premeditation and in the perpetration of the kidnapping. Although the rape was based on circumstantial evidence, sufficient evidence existed that defendant raped the victim and murdered her in the perpetration of the rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court and the sentence of death imposed by the jury.

Dicken v. State


No. M2003-01455-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 556


January 27, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
June 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Dicken v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 1000 (Tenn., Nov. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sumner County. No. 341-2002. Jane W. Wheatcraft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Sumner County (Tennessee), denying his petition for post-conviction relief, after he entered pleas of guilt to three counts of incest, a Class C felony. The trial court had denied alternative sentencing, citing petitioner's extensive criminal history and the need to avoid depreciating the seriousness of the offense, and there was no appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, petitioner argued that his trial counsel was ineffective by: (1) failing to conduct an adequate investigation of his statement, admitting that had been engaging in sexual intercourse with the victim; (2) failing to file a motion to suppress the statement; (3) failing to challenge the constitutionality of the incest statute (4) failing to object to the admission of the victim's videotaped statement at the sentencing hearing; and (5) going forward with the sentencing hearing without a psychosexual evaluation. The appellate court held that trial counsel's performance was not deficient because: (1) petitioner had assured counsel that what he told police was true, accurate, voluntary, and not the result of coercion; (2) petitioner had informed counsel that he never would be able to raise the $ 100 needed to pay an examiner for a psychosexual evaluation, and the results of a favorable evaluation would not have changed the outcome of the sentence; (3) the victim's videotaped statement was admissible as reliable hearsay; and (4) petitioner had not demonstrated that the incest statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Wong

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 553


March 9, 2004, Session  
June 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application denied by State v. Wong, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 1087 (Tenn., Dec. 6, 2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Chi-Choi Wong v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 319 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 7, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Chi-Choi Wong v. Lindamood, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18325 (M.D. Tenn., Feb. 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2000-D-1879. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that convicted him of promoting prostitution and of money laundering under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-512 and 39-14-903(b)(1), and sentenced him to 24 years. Defendant claimed the trial court erred in admitting evidence found in his apartment; in denying his motion to sever the offenses and to suppress evidence; and in imposing an excessive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted based on a four-month investigation in which confidential informants were used to apply for employment with defendant and to procure an "escort" through his service that was paid in exchange for sexual activity. Detailed records of the prostitution business were found in defendant's apartment. The court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court rejected defendant's hearsay claim as to the evidence because it was admitted only as circumstantial evidence of prostitution activity. The court also held that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-512 and 39-14-903(b)(1) were not vague or overly broad. The court concluded that the record amply supported the finding that the sentences were to run consecutively where defendant was a professional criminal and continued his business even after being arrested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Williams v. Mills


No. W2004-00056-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 461



May 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Williams v. Mills, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 714 (Tenn., Aug. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 5807. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.
State v. Williams, 1988 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 798 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 28, 1988)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee), which denied him habeas corpus relief. The matter was before the court on appellee State's motion to affirm the judgment by order pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of armed robbery. His petitions for post-conviction relief were denied. He then sought habeas corpus relief, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court properly determined that the inmate's claims were not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding. There was nothing to indicate that the lower court was without jurisdiction to sentence the inmate, nor was there anything to indicate that the inmate's sentences had expired. Thus, no grounds existed that entitled the inmate to habeas corpus relief under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15 or Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-101 et seq. The inmate's challenge to the selection process for the foreperson of the grand jury could only be addressed in a petition for post-conviction relief. Considering the inmate's application as one for post-conviction relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-105(c) (2003), the court concluded that the petition was barred as a petition for post-conviction relief because it was filed outside of the applicable statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and affirmed.

State v. Reagan


No. M2002-01472-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 452


September 17, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
May 19, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Reagan v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 70 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Overton County. No. 4594. Lillie Ann Sells, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Overton County (Tennessee) of first degree, premeditated murder and first degree murder by placing or discharging a destructive device or bomb. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his premeditated murder conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. A witness testified that he gave dynamite to defendant. Another witness testified that defendant told him that he was having marital problems and that he believed the victim (defendant's wife) was having an affair. The victim's mother testified that she believed the victim was going to leave defendant. While defendant was in jail after the explosion, defendant told an inmate that the victim deserved to die because she was having an affair. Several witnesses at the scene of the explosion testified that the victim was screaming from the pain and was afraid she was going to die. Defendant, unlike the victim, was calm after the explosion and wrapped a cord and a sweater around his arm to control the bleeding. Based on the experts' opinions, the victim's statements after the explosion, and defendant's actions, a jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was upset with the victim because she was having an affair and that he brought the dynamite with him into the car, intending to use the dynamite to kill the victim.


OUTCOME: The case was modified and remanded for entry of a single judgment for first degree murder. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Muhammed


No. E2003-01629-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 417


January 27, 2004, Argued  
May 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Muhammad, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 309 (Tenn., Mar. 12, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Muhammad v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 122 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 18, 2009)
Related proceeding at Muhammad v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1078 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 9, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Muhammad v. Donahue, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 107811 (E.D. Tenn., Aug. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 239344, 239483. Stephen M. Bevil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) of attempted second degree murder, two counts of aggravated assault, and attempted voluntary manslaughter. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the court erred by admitting a tape of a phone conversation between defendant and the victim, his wife. The court of appeals disagreed. During the victim's testimony, an audiotape was played for the jury, which was a recording made by the victim of a telephone conversations she had with defendant. Among his many profanity-laced comments were that she "ought to pay" for all she had put him through; that he was "liable to take his son and be gone;" and that he would "take it out on the victim's mother." Asked by the victim not to hurt their child, defendant replied, "that ain't my kid." Although the trial court determined that the audiotape of the conversations was admissible pursuant to Tenn. R. Evid. 803, the hearing conducted on the matter substantially complied with the requirements of Tenn. R. Evid. 404(b). The trial court conducted the appropriate jury-out hearing and stated that the probative value of the statements outweighed their prejudicial effect. The trial court explained that the audiotape of defendant's statements was admissible to show the required intent for the offense of attempt to commit first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gentry

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 416

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of aggravated rape. The court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. The victim testified that, when she woke up during the night of the rape, defendant had his hands inside her shorts and his fingers inside her and that she felt a "pinch" or "scrape" approximately one inch inside her vagina. The nurse also testified that the victim complained of some discomfort in her private parts and, when the nurse performed the examination, it was very painful for the victim. The nurse testified that the victim's injuries were consistent with the penetration of the victim's vagina by a finger.

State v. Myers


No. M2003-01099-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 390


February 3, 2004, Session  
April 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by State v. Myers, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 924 (Tenn., Nov. 8, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Myers v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 700 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 23, 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Myers v. Tennessee, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41218 (M.D. Tenn., Mar. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County. No. 01-0401A. John Turnbull, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of three counts of first degree murder, two counts of felony murder, one count of aggravated arson, and one count of conspiracy to commit murder. After a sentencing hearing, the Circuit Court for Putnam County (Tennessee) imposed consecutive sentences of life without the possibility of parole for each murder conviction, and a consecutive 24 year sentence for the aggravated arson conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions. Given the testimony concerning the injuries to the victims and the cause of the fire, the evidence clearly supported a finding that the killings were premeditated and intentional. The evidence reflected that the fire was intentionally set with the use of accelerants. The pathologist testified that two of the victims were alive at the time the fire was set. That was sufficient to support a finding that aggravated arson was committed. The appellate court concluded that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the findings of guilt. Inter alia, shortly before the murders, defendant threatened to harm one of the victims, even saying "he was going to burn her house down with her in it." A police officer testified that, when he asked defendant about tools, defendant mentioned the torque wrench and described exactly where investigators found it at the crime scene. However, several witnesses who had been in the house the day before the murders testified that there was no torque wrench in the living room at that time. While not overwhelming, the proof was sufficient to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

741 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Linsey


No. M2002-01299-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 376


February 3, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
April 16, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 40100547. Michael R. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to simple possession of cocaine in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Tennessee. Per his plea agreement, he expressly reserved, with the consent of the trial court and the State, the right to appeal a certified question of law pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37(b)(2), same being whether the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence that was seized as a result of a stop for a traffic violation.


OVERVIEW: For unknown reasons, an officer turned his vehicle around to follow defendant. When defendant turned, he failed to use his turn signal. The officer then effected a traffic stop. The officer then requested consent to search defendant's person and vehicle. Defendant gave consent only as to the search of his person, which revealed a bag of cocaine. In his motion to suppress, defendant asserted the officer did not have probable cause to believe that he had committed a crime. Defendant cited precedent for the proposition that the failure to use one's turn signal was not a traffic violation, unless it could have affected other motorists. In fact, defendant was correct that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 55-8-142(a) and 55-8-143(a) did not require a motorist to use a turn signal unless other traffic could be affected by the failure to use a turn signal under the circumstances. However, Clarksville, Tenn., City Ordinance § 9-401, which applied in defendant's case, mandated the use of a turn signal, and its additional requirement did not conflict with State law. Therefore, the officer had probable cause to stop defendant and there was no Fourth Amendment violation.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress and his conviction were affirmed.

 

742 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Orr


No. M2002-02332-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 326


September 16, 2003, Session  
April 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Tenn. v. Paul E. Orr, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 896 (Tenn., Oct. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marshall County. No. 14474. Charles Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence (DUI) in the Circuit Court for Marshall County, Tennessee. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss his DUI conviction, arguing that Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403(n) was unconstitutional because it applied only to certain urban counties. The trial court agreed and held that the statute violated equal protection rights afforded by the United States and Tennessee Constitutions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403(n) provided, in pertinent part, that in counties with a metropolitan form of government and a population in excess of 100,000, the judge could sentence a person convicted of violating Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401 for the first time to perform 200 hours of public service work in lieu of the minimum period of confinement. Defendant was convicted in Marshall County, but the latter statute applied to counties such as neighboring Davidson County. On appeal, the State contended that § 55-10-403(n) was constitutional because a rational basis existed for allowing trial courts in counties with populations over 100,000 (here Davidson County) to allow first-time DUI offenders to perform public service instead of serving a mandatory 48 hours in jail. The appellate court, applying its prior ruling in a similar case, State v. Ladonna Kay Lambert, held that, even if § 55-10-403(n) were unconstitutional, § 55-10-403(n) had to be elided from Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403. That left the general DUI sentencing law in effect. Thus, the trial court erred by ruling on the constitutionality of the provision and by holding that the entire statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court dismissing defendant's conviction was reversed, and the matter was remanded for disposition consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

McGowan v. State


No. M2003-00268-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at McGowan v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 545 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 7, 2004)
Appeal denied by McGowan v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 1004 (Tenn., Nov. 15, 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed McGowan v. Bell, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1016 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 21, 2006)
Related proceeding at McGowan v. State, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 858 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 31, 2007)
Related proceeding at McGowan v. State, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 341 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 16, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed McGowan v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1037 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 00C-3729. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, inmate, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition of writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate received a sentence of 20-years for aggravated arson, five years for arson, and one year on each of the eight remaining counts involving reckless endangerment with a deadly weapon and vandalism. All sentences were ordered to run concurrently with the 20-year sentence for aggravated arson. The judgment also reflected that the 20-year sentence was ordered to run concurrently with a prior, apparently unrelated case in a second county. The record was devoid of any details concerning the case in the second county. The inmate argued that the sentence was void because it was ordered to run concurrent to the prior unrelated offense, in contravention of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-111(b). The appellate court ruled that it was unable to ascertain from the record whether the inmate was out on bond on the prior case when any of the other felony offenses were committed. Included in the plea agreement was the provision that all of the sentences would be served concurrently. However, as the trial judge did not hold a hearing on the issue, the appellate court could not resolve it on the record before it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Bryant v. State


No. E2002-00907-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 231


April 30, 2003, Argued  
March 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Bryant v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 789 (Tenn., Sept. 7, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bryant v. Tennessee, 125 S. Ct. 1314, 161 L. Ed. 2d 111, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1503 (U.S., 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Bryant v. Carlton, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1390 (E.D. Tenn., Jan. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Greene County. No. 01-CR-161. James Edward Beckner, Judge.
Risner v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 575 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Greene County (Tennessee) to three counts of first degree murder and one count of attempted first degree murder. The court dismissed defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his trial counsel was ineffective because he did not prevent the transfer of defendant to the criminal court from juvenile court. The court of appeals disagreed. Counsel filed a motion contesting the transfer to the criminal court. The juvenile court denied that motion. Counsel testified that his strategy was to establish that defendant was not the shooter, contrary to the contention of the other five defendants. Therefore, he opposed an extensive mental evaluation because he did not want defendant available to the State's psychiatrists. He was afraid that due to defendant's mental history that the State would prove that defendant was a "compulsive psychopath." Counsel testified that he did not believe there was anything he could do to prevent the transfer to criminal court. Part of the trial counsel's strategy was to prevent the appearance that defendant was a psychopath by not delving into his mental health history. Therefore, the trial counsel did not want an extensive mental evaluation prepared for that phase of the prosecution. That was a reasonable strategy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

745 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pillow


No. M2002-01864-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 176


August 13, 2003, Session  
February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Pillow, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 596 (Tenn., June 21, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Pillow v. State, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 459 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Maury County. No. 11850. Robert L. Jones, Judge.
State v. Price, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 332 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Maury County (Tennessee) of second degree murder, two counts of facilitation of attempted first degree murder, three counts of facilitation of attempted especially aggravated robbery, reckless endangerment, and facilitation of aggravated burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction for facilitation of attempted first degree murder. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence established that defendant traveled to a residence with his accomplices to rob the victims. All three carried weapons. Defendant was an active participant and was the first to fire his weapon during the confrontation, arguably escalating the gravity of the situation. Although robbery was the intended crime, the jury could have inferred that the intended crime became murder when an accomplice shouted at the others to kill one of the victims. Two of the victims, neither of whom were armed, suffered terrible injury as a result of gunshot wounds received in the fray. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions for facilitation of attempted first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

746 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Crawford v. State


No. E2003-00097-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


151 S.W.3d 179; 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1171


November 18, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Crawford v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 615 (Tenn., June 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. C46,282 R. Jerry Beck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee) to six counts of attempt to commit incest and six counts of attempt to commit rape. Petitioner's motion for postconviction relief was denied. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in dismissing his post-conviction petition with regard to deoyribonucleic acid (DNA) analysis issues without a hearing. The court of appeals disagreed. The comforter and the quilt were tested in 1995 before the petitioner entered his Alford plea. The testing clearly showed that petitioner's DNA was on the comforter or the quilt. Additional testing proving that someone else's sperm was on the comforter or quilt would not lessen the potential of his guilt when his DNA was found in the original tests. In addition, based upon what petitioner's counsel stated, it was unlikely that additional tests would show that petitioner's sperm was present on the comforter from having sex with his ex-wife. According to what the forensic scientist told petitioner's counsel, it was unlikely that it would show his ex-wife's DNA and even more likely that it would show more of his DNA. Those facts did not lead to a reasonable probability to allow further DNA testing and possible tolling of the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Thomas


No. W2001-02701-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 185


November 4, 2003 Session  
February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bond, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 719 (Tenn., Aug. 30, 2004)
Affirmed by State v. Thomas, 158 S.W.3d 361, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 135 (Tenn., 2005)
Appeal after remand at State v. Bond, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 724 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 20, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Thomas v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 131 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 23, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bond v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 68 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 24, 2013)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Thomas v. Colson, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 140151 (W.D. Tenn., Sept. 30, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Certificate of appealability granted, in part, Certificate of appealability denied, in part Thomas v. United States, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 113589 (W.D. Tenn., Aug. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as to Defendant Thomas; Reversed and Remanded as to Defendant Bond. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 00-03095. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.
United States v. Bond, 29 Fed. Appx. 241, 2002 U.S. App. LEXIS 1873 (6th Cir. Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed as to Defendant Thomas; Reversed and Remanded as to Defendant Bond.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted by a jury in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of first-degree murder, as to one defendant, and felony murder, as to the other defendant. The defendant who was convicted of first-degree murder was sentenced to death. The defendant who was convicted of felony murder was sentenced to life without the possibility of parole. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: One defendant admitted that he and the other defendant took part in the robbery of an armored truck and that the victim was shot in the back of the head during the commission of the robbery. Furthermore, witnesses identified one defendant and testified as to defendants' admissions and their spending of the stolen money. The victim was paralyzed and suffered medical complications. Two-and-a-half years later, the victim died from an infection as a direct result of the gunshot wound. On appeal, the court found that, with regard to the defendant convicted of first-degree murder, the evidence supported the conviction, the sentence of death was not imposed in any arbitrary fashion, and the evidence supported the jury's finding that the aggravating circumstance outweighed mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. Furthermore, the sentence of death was neither excessive nor disproportionate. With regard to the defendant convicted of felony murder, the trial court's failure to properly charge the jury as to the lesser-included offense of facilitation of felony murder was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, that defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The jury's verdict finding one defendant guilty of first-degree murder and imposing the sentence of death was affirmed. The jury's verdict finding the other defendant guilty of felony murder and imposing the sentence of life without the possibility of parole was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

 

748 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Cauthern v. State


No. M2002-00929-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


145 S.W.3d 571; 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 149


April 22, 2003, Session  
February 19, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 40000059. Michael R. Jones, Judge.
State v. Cauthern, 967 S.W.2d 726, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 161 (Tenn., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) of two counts of felony murder, first-degree burglary, and aggravated rape. He was sentenced to death, both in his first and second sentencing trials. His convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. The trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for postconviction relief, as counsel's failure to investigate and present mitigating evidence about his family background and troubled childhood was not an informed strategic decision. The court of appeals disagreed. Counsel's mitigation preparation did not consist solely of interviews with the defendant. Counsel sought family history, but the people interviewed were very "guarded" in providing information about defendant's biological mother and father. Counsel arranged for a sanity and competency evaluation before the first trial. Defendant was declared competent to stand trial, and an insanity defense could not be supported. Doctors came to the same conclusion as a result of their examinations. Whether the evaluation before the first trial generated any useful or alarming insights into defendant's mental history beyond competency and sanity was unknown. The evidence failed to preponderate against the trial court's finding that counsel's investigation and representation was within the wide range of professionally competent assistance. In addition, defendant was unable to show prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Swiggett v. Carlton


No. E2003-02212-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 123



February 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Swiggett v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 383 (Tenn., May 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Johnson County. No. 4153. Robert E. Cupp, Judge.
Swiggett v. State, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 861 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 15, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Johnson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The State filed a motion requesting that the court affirm the trial court's denial of relief pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner alleged that the Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989, under which he was convicted and sentenced, was unconstitutional under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 17 because it embraced more than one subject, not reflected in the title. The court held that any defect in the caption was cured by the codification in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-101 et seq. The Act was thus not unconstitutional, and the prisoner's subsequent judgment was not void. Although the prisoner sought remand of his case to the court of conviction for further proceedings, the sole relief available under Tennessee's habeas corpus statute was discharge from custody.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Mack


No. W2002-01828-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


188 S.W.3d 164; 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 44


July 9, 2003, Session  
January 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Shaw, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 611 (Tenn., June 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Reversed and Dismissed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 7237. Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee) of possession of more than 0.5 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the convictions. The court of appeals agreed. There were no drugs or money found on defendant's person. Her presence in the area where drugs were found did not suffice to prove her possession. However, the State presented evidence that the other defendant had $ 395 in cash at the time he was searched and that the cocaine possessed by another individual had a value of approximately $ 380. A rational trier of fact could have inferred that defendant had recently possessed the cocaine prior to selling it to the other individual. An equally rational trier of fact could have inferred that defendant intended to buy the cocaine possessed by the other. In any event, in light of the finding that the evidence seized pursuant to the defective search warrant should have been suppressed, the money possessed by defendant was inadmissible "fruit" of the unconstitutional search. Therefore, the evidence was insufficient to sustain the convictions.


OUTCOME: The convictions were reversed and dismissed.

Ross v. State


No. W2003-01448-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



January 9, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Ross v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 415 (Tenn., May 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-26913. J.C. McLin, Judge.
State v. Ross, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 62 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 28, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Motion granted; judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied the prisoner coram nobis relief. The State filed a motion to affirm the judgment of the trial court by order pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of attempted murder, aggravated robbery, and theft. After the convictions and sentences were affirmed and post-conviction relief was denied, petitioner sought a writ of error coram nobis relief. Petitioner asserted that he should be granted a new trial based upon grounds of newly discovered evidence. Specifically, petitioner claimed that a codefendant was willing to provide an affidavit and testimony that petitioner was not an accomplice in the commission of the criminal acts. The court held that, to the extent that petitioner sought the benefit of a writ of error coram nobis, his claim was time barred, because it was not filed within one year from the judgment's finality under Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-7-103. Moreover, petitioner had not demonstrated the applicability of any basis upon which he could be excused from the statute of limitations bar. The codefendant's recantation would not have had an impact on the result of the trial. The codefendant's credibility was effectively questioned at trial. A police officer identified petitioner as being in the get-away vehicle, and stolen items were discovered at petitioner's home and in the car.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Reid


No. M2001-02753-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1086


October 14, 2003, Session  
December 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 1, 2005.
Application denied by Reid v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 1268 (Tenn., Oct. 4, 2004)
Appeal denied by Reid v. State, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 161 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)
Affirmed by State v. Reid, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 481 (Tenn., May 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 38887. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.
State v. Reid, 91 S.W.3d 247, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 550 (Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) of two counts of premeditated murder, two counts of felony murder, two counts of especially aggravated kidnapping, and one count of especially aggravated robbery. The felony murder convictions were merged into the premeditated murder convictions. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in admitting the videotape of the crime scene into evidence, because it was cumulative and it was "gruesome and graphic." The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court found that the video aided the jury in understanding the testimony of medical examiners, crime scene investigators, and witnesses. The trial court noted that the jury was from Memphis and presumably unfamiliar with the area and Dunbar Cave State Park. The trial court also found that the video depicted the location of the bodies and was shown to document the position of the bodies in relation to the lake, the trail described by investigators and witnesses, the parking lot, and the cave. The trial court determined that the video was not "particularly gruesome." Defendant advanced the argument that the video was graphic and gruesome only because the video showed the bodies of the victims as they were found at the crime scene. The crime scene video of most murders necessarily depicted the bodies of the victims as they were found. While the videotape and the other evidence might have contained some of the same material, it was not error to admit the videotape.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

753 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mullins


No. M2002-02977-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1091


October 14, 2003, Session  
December 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Mullins, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 513 (Tenn., June 1, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Mullins v. State, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 982 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 19, 2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Mullins v. Lindamood, 2017 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 679 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County. No. 99-0599. Leon Burns, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Putnam County, convicted defendant of felony murder, second degree murder, especially aggravated robbery and especially aggravated burglary, and immediately sentenced defendant to life without parole on the first degree felony murder count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was robbed in her home and killed by suffocation. Fibers taken from her carpet matched those found on defendant's person. A witness testified that defendant was seen with a ring stolen from the victim and that defendant needed money to buy crack cocaine. He was convicted for the crime. The appellate court found the evidence sufficient to support defendant's conviction for felony murder, second degree murder, especially aggravated robbery and especially aggravated burglary. The jury was properly instructed that it was only necessary to find that every element of the offense be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The trial court did not err in instructing the jury that it was permitted to consider aggravating circumstances; the instruction matched the requirements of the Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(f)(1), (2) & (i). Defendant's complaint regarding the use of aggravating circumstances that were not alleged in the indictment lacked merit. Tennessee's sentencing scheme for life imprisonment without parole was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

754 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shortt


No. E2002-02184-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1054



December 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Shortt, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 463 (Tenn., May 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hawkins County No. 8024 James E. Beckner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Criminal Court for Hawkins County (Tennessee), after he was convicted of manufacturing marijuana, a Class D felony, and possession of drug paraphernalia, a Class A misdemeanor. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of two years and 11 months, 29 days, respectively.


OVERVIEW: While piloting a helicopter, a sheriff's department lieutenant observed what he believed to be several marijuana plants growing on property owned by defendant. After obtaining a search warrant based upon this surveillance, officers seized 17 marijuana plants, scales, plastic baggies, and other paraphernalia. Defendant raised three issues on appeal. The appellate court held that: (1) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress, because defendant had no reasonable expectation that the marijuana plants on his property were protected from observation by police flying in a helicopter at an altitude of 1,700 feet, the marijuana plants seized from defendant's property did not fall within the curtilage of defendant's residence and were, therefore, subject to seizure under the "open fields" doctrine, and aerial photographs introduced by defendant's private investigator at trial did not qualify as newly discovered evidence; (2) the evidence was sufficient for a reasonable jury to find defendant guilty of manufacturing between 10 and 19 marijuana plants; and (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by ordering a sentence of confinement.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

755 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thacker


No. W2002-01119-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1133


July 8, 2003, Session  
December 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Thacker, 164 S.W.3d 208, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 366 (Tenn., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Thacker v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 186 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified. Dyer County No. C00-54; Lake County No. 01-CR-8238. R. Lee Moore, Jr., Judge. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Courts for Dyer and Lake Counties.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Dyer County (Tennessee) of first-degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. Although defendant contended that he did not procure the knife to kill the victim, the jury could have inferred that defendant was armed to kill the victim or any other individual who interfered with his flight from capture. Defendant's actions after stabbing the victim exhibited a coolness of purpose and a calculating demeanor. Defendant dragged the victim's body out of sight. He then removed personal belongings, including a gun, cash, and credit cards from the victim. Then, recognizing that he was unable to remove a vehicle from the victim's tow truck, defendant proceeded to drive the tow truck to a secluded location, where he eventually unloaded the vehicle. Defendant then proceeded to purchase a hamburger from a Wendy's drive-thru and visit a local AutoZone, before securing a different vehicle and obtaining a motel room in Union City. Upon a search of defendant's motel room, a bottle of men's hair dye was found. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to show that defendant's convictions for first-degree premeditated murder and first-degree felony murder were merged into one judgment. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

756 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Guthrie v. State


No. M2003-00832-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1035


September 17, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
December 11, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Guthrie v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 508 (Tenn., June 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lincoln County. No. S0300037. Charles Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition in the Circuit Court for Lincoln County, Tennessee, for post-conviction relief, alleging that proof of counsel's substance abuse was a late-arising claim that involved due process concerns. The trial court dismissed the petition as untimely. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner had pleaded guilty to attempted second-degree murder and voluntary manslaughter. Nearly more than four years later, his counsel was placed on probationary status by the bar association and was required to undergo treatment for substance abuse. On appeal, the prisoner argued that proof of counsel's substance abuse was a late-arising claim that involved due process concerns. He also challenged his hybrid sentence as to voluntary manslaughter as illegal and unconstitutional. The appellate court noted that due process prohibited the strict application of the post-conviction statute of limitations, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a), when the grounds for relief arose after the point at which the limitations period would normally have begun to run. The appellate court held that alcohol or drug abuse by a defense attorney, without specific proof of its effect on performance, did not merit relief. The appellate court further held that offender classification and release eligibility were non-jurisdictional and were legitimate bargaining tools under the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Gailes


No. W2002-02080-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1019


November 4, 2003, Session  
December 3, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Appeal Dismissed. No. 00-12589. J.C. McLin, Judge. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to fourth offense driving under the influence, reserving a certified question of law in which he challenged the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403 as applied. The Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) imposed a two-year sentence with all but 150 days suspended and certified defendant's question. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his certified question defendant claimed that Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-10-403(a)(3) operated in an unconstitutionally retrospective manner as it applied to his 1988 convictions for driving under the influence. If the statute were found to be unconstitutional as applied, he should only have been prosecuted for a second offense of driving while intoxicated. The court held that it was without jurisdiction to hear the appeal because the certified question did not dispose of all issues in the case. Defendant conceded that the relief he sought would not have resulted in the dismissal of the indictment; rather, the court would have had to remand the case for reconsideration of the charge of driving under the influence as a second offense. Therefore, under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37(b)(2) the court was without jurisdiction to hear the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

758 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cole


No. W2002-01254-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1002


September 9, 2003, Session  
November 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Tenn. v. Detrick Cole, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 15 (Tenn., Jan. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. No. 01-01221. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of premeditated first-degree murder. The jury found that the State had proven beyond a reasonable doubt the Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2) aggravating circumstance, defendant was previously convicted of one or more violent felonies, and that the aggravating circumstance outweighed any mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asked the victim to go behind an apartment complex. Unsatisfied with the victim's refusal to pay a debt, defendant shot him above the left eye and above the left ear from a distance of less than an inch. Defendant escaped in the victim's car, discarded the weapon, and twice returned to search for his electronic pocket organizer. The court concluded that a rational trier of fact could have found that defendant intentionally and premeditatedly killed the victim. Post-mortem photographs of the victim were relevant to show that the wound was inflicted from contact range, from which a jury could infer premeditation and which dispelled defendant's claim of self-defense. Fingerprinting of defendant in the presence of the jury during the penalty phase of the trial was not so inflammatory or prejudicial as to render the trial fundamentally unfair. Any error in not allowing the jury to make the determination that defendant's prior felonies involved violence was harmless. Any rational juror would have found that the offenses, which all involved a firearm pointed at the victim, were violent felonies. The State's evidence was sufficient to establish the aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the premeditated first-degree murder conviction and the sentence of death.

State v. Brewer


No. M2002-02749-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 957


July 16, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
November 13, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Maury County. Nos. 12425, 12864. Stella Hargrove, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Maury County, Tennessee, revoking his probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to aggravated burglary, theft over $ 1000, and vandalism and was sentenced to five years probation. After defendant tested positive for marijuana and his probation officer filed a probation violation report, the trial court revoked his probation following a hearing. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in relying upon a laboratory report showing marijuana in his urine because the accompanying affidavit had not been executed by the technician who performed the test but by the assistant laboratory director. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-311(c)(1) set forth the requirements for admission of a laboratory report at a probation revocation proceeding. It did not require an affidavit from the technician who performed the test. In this case, the affiant was the assistant laboratory director; his affidavit was sufficient to satisfy the requirements of § 40-35-311(c)(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

760 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Prater


No. E2002-01774-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


137 S.W.3d 25; 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 886


April 29, 2003, Session  
October 17, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Prater, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 169 (Tenn., Mar. 1, 2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Prater v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 26 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as fo Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rhea County. No. 15552. J. Curtis Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Rhea County (Tennessee) of aggravated child abuse, and fined $ 25,000. As a result of the conviction, the trial court sentenced her to 21 years and six months incarceration as a range I, standard offender and classified her release eligibility at 100 percent as a violent offender. After the trial court denied appellant's motion for a new trial, she appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State was required to prove that appellant, in giving her child a double dose of Clonidine, knowingly treated the child in an abusive manner, not that she merely knowingly gave him medication. The child abuse statutes were not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant because the statutes required that appellant knew her conduct was abusive. Also, the proof introduced at trial established that the child was taking Clonidine, and that five days after the prescription was written, appellant called the doctor's office three times in one day asking if she could increase the dosage. Each time appellant called, she was told that she was "absolutely not" to increase the dosage, but appellant admitted that she gave the child twice the prescribed dosage. Two days later, the child's father and aunt took him to the emergency room, where he exhibited signs and symptoms of Clonidine toxicity. A rational jury could have concluded that appellant knowingly gave her child twice his dosage of Clonidine against the instructions of medical professionals and that appellant knew her actions were abusive. The evidence supported the jury's finding of guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
