Mann v. State


No. W2002-00260-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 858


January 7, 2003 Session  
October 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mann v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 210 (Tenn., Mar. 8, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at Mann v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1032 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dyer County. No. C93-337, 338. Russell Lee Moore, Jr., Judge
State v. Mann, 959 S.W.2d 503, 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 608 (Tenn., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Dyer County (Tennessee) of murder and sentenced to death. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for postconviction relief, because counsel was ineffective for failing to conduct a sufficient investigation of the case. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court found that the local district attorney had an open file policy and that the file along with the statements of the officers and the investigation of the case were available to defendant's attorneys and investigators. The trial court found that there was no evidence to suggest an insufficient investigation as a basis for an ineffective assistance of counsel claim nor any evidence to suggest prejudice in terms of guilt or innocence. In connection with the sentencing phase of the trial, the trial court found that there was no real mitigation evidence. As part of trial strategy, trial counsel chose not to use an expert, because she indicated that she would hurt their case. Additionally, defendant failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that he was prejudiced, and evidence that additional mitigation investigation would have caused a different result in sentencing was insufficient for defendant to carry his burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

762 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. W2003-02344-CCA-R10-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 874



October 6, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Criminal Court for Shelby County, No. 99-13438.
State v. Wilson, 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 651 (Tenn. Ct. App., Sept. 4, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order reversed and vacated; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of felony murder and second-degree murder. He appealed. The case was remanded as the trial court failed to instruct as to the lesser-included offenses of premeditated first-degree murder and felony murder. On remand, the Shelby County Criminal Court, Division V (Tennessee), refused to instruct any lesser included offense of felony murder. Defendant's application for an extraordinary appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: On retrial, the trial court granted the State's motion, declaring the Tennessee Supreme Court decision in Ely unconstitutional in that it violated the doctrine of separation of powers. The appellate court held that the law of the case doctrine prevented the State from seeking to change its position regarding the propriety of charging lesser-included offenses. The prosecution had the obligation to raise the constitutional challenge on direct appeal. The instant court's previous decision impliedly found the supreme court's decision in Ely not violative of the constitutional doctrine of separation of powers. Further, the supreme court's ruling defining lesser offenses under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-18-110 was not an unconstitutional abuse of the judiciary's power and did not constitute an infringement of the legislative branch's power to define criminal offenses. The General Assembly had the authority to define lesser offenses of the greater indicted offense. While directing trial courts to instruct on lesser offenses, the General Assembly failed to delineate what offenses were to be considered lesser offenses. Thus, the supreme court had the authority and the duty to intervene.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order declaring the supreme court's decision in Ely unconstitutional, and refusing to instruct on applicable lesser offenses was reversed, vacated, and remanded. Specifically, the trial court was ordered, upon retrial, to instruct the jury as to all lesser included offenses of second-degree murder and felony murder.

 

763 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Faulkner


No. W2001-02614-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 836


May 6, 2003, Session  
September 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Faulkner, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 40 (Tenn., Jan. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 99-07635. Chris Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder. The jury found one aggravating circumstance pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2), that defendant had been previously convicted of one or more violent felonies. The jury determined that the aggravating circumstance outweighed any mitigating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he killed his estranged wife, but claimed that he acted in a state of passion. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding expert testimony on diminished capacity, as the witness was unable to testify that defendant lacked the capacity to premeditate or to act intentionally or knowingly because of a mental disease or defect. Photographs demonstrating repeated blows to the head of the victim were relevant to show premeditation. Although the verdict form did not require the jury to note that the aggravating circumstances were found beyond a reasonable doubt, the jury could only have understood the burden of proof to apply to the determination of aggravating circumstances. Any error regarding an "intentionally" instruction was harmless, because the jury could find that defendant caused the death of the victim. An indictment sufficiently charged first-degree murder as the death penalty was within the statutory range of punishment. No international law prohibited the death penalty, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(c) did not violate separation of powers. The sentence was not disproportionate to that imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

764 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibson


No. E2002-01533-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 777


February 25, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
September 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Gibson, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 126 (Tenn., Feb. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sevier County. No. 8457. Rex Henry Ogle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Sevier County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of driving under the influence and failure to carry a driver's license. He was sentenced him to 90 days of incarceration, followed by supervised probation, and his license was suspended for two years. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review of his conviction for driving under the influence and failing carry a driver's license, defendant claimed: (1) the trial court erred in failing to suppress all evidence gained as a result of his traffic stop; and (2) the trial court erred by admitting into evidence the results of his breathalyzer test. The appellate court found no reversible error. The officer's stop of defendant's car was justified by reasonable suspicion provided by an informant who called police stating that a car matching the description of defendant's vehicle was driving erratically. Therefore, evidence obtained during the stop was not subject to suppression. Defendant waived any issue regarding the admission into evidence of the breathalyzer test results at trial by his failure to make a timely objection. Counsel for defendant was permitted to refer to the breathalyzer test results in the opening statement. The arresting officer's testimony laid the foundation for admission of the test results.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lauderdale


No. W2001-01296-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 783


March 4, 2003, Session  
September 5, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lauderdale, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 99 (Tenn., Jan. 26, 2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Lauderdale v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 866 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. No. 13058 Julian P. Guinn, Judge. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Henry County.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Henry County (Tennessee), after he was convicted by a jury of first degree felony murder, and the trial court sentenced him as a violent offender to life in the Tennessee Department of Correction.


OVERVIEW: The case related to the death of the seven-year-old child of defendant's girlfriend. When an officer arrived at the scene, the victim was unresponsive in an ambulance and appeared to have burn marks on the left side of her face and neck. Defendant raised four issues on appeal. The appellate court held that: (1) the evidence was sufficient, because a witness testified that defendant whipped the victim in the bathroom, brought the victim into the living room, lifted the victim over his head, and slammed the victim onto the floor, and defendant then splashed hot water on the victim in an attempt to revive her, put her into bed, and left the apartment; (2) the indictment provided defendant with sufficient notice, as aggravated child abuse and aggravated child neglect were not separate felonies, and the jury's verdict was unanimous; (3) the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress, accrediting officers' testimony that defendant did not request an attorney; and (4) defendant was not denied his right to a fair trial, because there was no cumulative error and defendant waived his other fair trial issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

766 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leach


No. M2001-01421-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 724


February 11, 2003, Argued  
August 25, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Leach, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 741 (Tenn., Sept. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 99-D-2508. J. Randall Wyatt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of premeditated murder, two counts of felony murder, one count of aggravated rape, and one count of especially aggravated robbery. The felony murder convictions were merged into the premeditated murder convictions. Defendant received the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his first-degree premeditated murder conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant used two weapons, scissors and a ligature, on unarmed victims. According to the evidence presented at trial, he inflicted multiple wounds to each victim during a very brutal attack. The evidence showed that he attempted to dispose of evidence of the murders by flushing his underwear down the toilet. Defendant was calm after the murders as he showered, changed his clothes, went through the victims' residence in search of valuables, washed his socks out in the sink, and flushed his underwear down the toilet. Moreover, after the murders, defendant drove to Missouri where he visited relatives and "partied" with friends. A witness testified that defendant told him that he committed the murders and explained that it was his fantasy to go on a rape and murder spree. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict of first-degree premeditated murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment referring to count 5 was actually for the aggravated rape conviction in count 6, and the judgment referring to count 6 was actually for the especially aggravated robbery conviction in count 5. The case was remanded for the trial court to correct those clerical errors. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

767 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCraney


No. W2003-00011-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 722


July 9, 2003, Session  
August 22, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Interlocutory Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dyer County. No. C02-102. Lee Moore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for various narcotics charges arising out of the search of his vehicle. The Circuit Court for Dyer County (Tennessee) suppressed the evidence obtained as a result of that search, ruling that the search of defendant's vehicle was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the State's motion for an interlocutory appeal. The appellate court granted the State permission to appeal the judgment granting the motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The officer testified that he witnessed defendant's car dive down as a result of unsafe breaking, which was caused by defendant's following the vehicle in front of him too closely in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-8-124(a) (1998). Conversely, defendant testified that his car did not dive down and that the reason for the rapid breaking was that the vehicle in front of him unexpectedly slowed almost to a stop. Defendant also presented evidence that the traffic stop might have been pretextual. The officer admitted that he was initially alerted to defendant's vehicle because of its Florida license plates. Thus, it was within the trial court's discretion to conclude that the officer had no reasonable suspicion to believe that defendant had violated § 55-8-124(a) and the trial court correctly ruled that the traffic stop was invalid. Thus, the trial court did not erroneously grant defendant's motion to suppress the evidence derived from the subsequent search of defendant's vehicle. Because the record was void of any evidence against defendant not obtained as a result of the initial traffic stop, the trial court properly suppressed the evidence and dismissed the case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

768 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. W2001-01299-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 694


May 6, 2003, Session  
August 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Robinson, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 60 (Tenn., Jan. 26, 2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by State v. Robinson, 146 S.W.3d 469, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 843 (Tenn., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Reversed; Remanded for New Trial. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 97-13179-80. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Wilkins, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 640 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 18, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) found defendant guilty of premeditated first-degree murder based upon the theory of criminal responsibility for the conduct of another and sentenced him to death. The jury also found him guilty of especially aggravated kidnapping and sentenced him to a 25 year consecutive sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant directed co-defendant to "take him (the victim) fishing." Co-defendant took him to a park where he and other gang members shot the victim to death. The appellate court addressed many issues raised by defendant on appeal, but it was the failure to charge on lesser-included offenses that led to the reversal of defendant's convictions. The appellate court found that the failure to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offenses of facilitation and solicitation as lesser-included offenses of premeditated first-degree murder was error, as the jury could have found that defendant did not share the intent to commit premeditated first-degree murder with the principals. The appellate court also found that the trial court failed to instruct the jury regarding facilitation and solicitation as lesser-included offenses of especially aggravated kidnapping, because the jury could have concluded that defendant ordered the gang members to "take him fishing," but that defendant did not intend for the kidnapping to be especially aggravated. Because the errors were not harmless, defendant was entitled to a new trial. Finally, the State could not seek the death penalty on remand.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

State v. Paris


No. E2002-01514-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 658


February 25, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
July 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Paris, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1246 (Tenn., Dec. 22, 2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Paris v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 863 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 16, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Paris v. Carlton, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 30206 (E.D. Tenn., Mar. 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 224116, 224232. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), after a jury found him guilty of first degree premeditated murder, first degree felony murder, and especially aggravated robbery. The two murder convictions merged, and the jury sentenced defendant to life without parole. The trial court sentenced defendant to 25 years for especially aggravated robbery, to run concurrently with a previous sentence.


OVERVIEW: The dead body of the victim was found in a dumpster. Fingerprints found at the scene led police to defendant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to suppress an incriminating statement he made, the jury charge regarding criminal responsibility was in error, and his sentencing was erroneous. The appellate court held that it was not error for the trial court to credit the testimony of a detective that defendant initiated contact with police and discredit the testimony of defendant, leading to the conclusion that the encounter at issue was not a custodial interrogation. Therefore, it was not error to fail to suppress the incriminating statement. Additionally, there was no error in the charge to the jury concerning criminal responsibility, because there was a theory that defendant shot the victim, and there was an alternate theory that another person shot the victim and defendant was criminally responsible for that person's actions. Finally, it was not a due process violation to use a prior conviction that occurred prior to the instant case's sentencing as satisfying the aggravating factor of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

770 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lockhart


No. W2002-02021-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 624


April 1, 2003 Session  
July 11, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County. No. 1894 C. Creed McGinley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Carroll County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of possession of less than .5 grams of methamphetamine with the intent to distribute, a Class C felony, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 37, defendant reserved as a certified question of law the issue of whether the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress. The police entered defendant's residence pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-7-107, which governed the authority of police officers to break into a residence in order to effectuate an arrest. The appellate court noted that the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that the officers acted within reasonable bounds and in accordance with the law. After knocking on the back door, identifying themselves, and receiving no response, the officers, who had seen vehicles parked outside the residence, opened the back door and heard a television. When they announced themselves a second time, they heard the affirmative reply, "Yeah." Defendant's reply could reasonably have been construed as consent to the officers' presence. Had the officers been denied entry, they could have lawfully broken into the residence in order to make an arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Risner v. State


No. E2002-01112-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 575

Post-conviction relief denied at, Sub nomine at Bryant v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 231 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 11, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Risner v. Tennessee, 160 L. Ed. 2d 44, 125 S. Ct. 214, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5791 (U.S., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Greene County. No. 01CR155. James E. Beckner, Judge.
State v. Howell, 34 S.W.3d 484, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 167 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the order of the Criminal Court for Greene County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a "package deal" plea, the inmate, along with five of his co-defendants, pled guilty to three counts of first-degree murder, one count of attempted murder, two counts of especially aggravated kidnapping, two counts of kidnapping, and one count of class D felony theft. The inmate presented the following issues for review: (1) whether his plea was knowingly and voluntarily entered; (2) whether he was denied the effective assistance of counsel; and (3) whether the indictment, which did not include the aggravating circumstances qualifying him for the death penalty, was unconstitutional. State v. Webb

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Webb, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1233 (Tenn., Dec. 15, 2003)
Appeal denied by State v. Webb, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 119 (Tenn., Feb. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded for Entry of a Corrected Judgment and for an Evidentiary Hearing as to Restitution. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. 00-643. Roger A. Page, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of the Circuit Court for Madison County (Tennessee), after they were convicted of 47 counts of cruelty to animals, sentenced to concurrent sentences with a prohibition from either owning animals for 10 years, ordered to pay restitution and perform community service, and fined. The trial court then found that each had possessed animals since their convictions and revoked their community corrections sentences.


OVERVIEW: The record on appeal established that defendants kept a large number of dogs in horrendous conditions. The appellate court initially noted that the jury foreperson mistakenly stated that defendants had been found guilty of count eight, although the form for that count showed that both were found not guilty. On appeal, defendants raised numerous arguments. The appellate court generally held that: (1) probable cause for a search warrant resulted from the nature of the complaints to a sergeant; (2) the sergeant did not intentionally or recklessly mislead the judge to obtain the search warrant; (3) Tenn. OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgments of the trial court, but remanded for entry of a corrected judgment showing that defendants were acquitted of count eight and for an evidentiary hearing as to the ordering of restitution.

State v. Orey


No. W2002-00482-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 532


January 7, 2003, Session  
June 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Orey, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1085 (Tenn., Oct. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County. No. 01CR1769. Roy Morgan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Carroll County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of DUI, third offense, and driving while license suspended, fifth offense. He was sentenced, respectively, to 11 months and 29 days, with all but 180 days suspended, and six months, with all but 45 days suspended, the sentences to be served concurrently. Defendant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: An officer "clocked" defendant's truck at a speed of 47 miles per hour in a 35 mile per hour zone. Defendant staggered out of his vehicle when it was stopped. The officer smelled alcohol on the defendant, and determined that his license had been revoked. Defendant refused to take a breathalyzer test. On review, defendant argued the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for third offense DUI and that his sentence for 11 months and 29 days was excessive. The appellate court disagreed. Defendant was not entitled a verdict of not guilty merely because he presented more witnesses than the State. Implicit in the jury's verdict was its finding that the State's witnesses, testifying that the defendant was intoxicated as he operated his truck, were credible. Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403(a)(1) required that a defendant be sentenced to a minimum period of confinement of 120 days. The trial court was permitted to use his prior California DUI convictions for enhancement purposes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Bates


No. M2002-01803-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 486


March 11, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
June 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bates, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1060 (Tenn., Oct. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hickman County. No. 97-5202CR-I. Russ Heldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Criminal Court for Hickman County (Tennessee), which denied his motion to be released from an outpatient treatment program after he was acquitted of several criminal charges by reason of insanity.


OVERVIEW: The patient was acquitted of several crimes by reason of insanity. He was ordered to participate in a mandatory outpatient treatment program under Tenn. Code Ann. § 33-7-303(a). Several years later, the patient filed a motion seeking release from the program because the State failed to renew his obligation under Tenn. Code Ann. § 33-6-621. After the trial court denied the motion, the patient sought review. In affirming, the court held that the trial court properly found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 33-7-303(a) applied to the case because it established the standard by which a person acquitted based on insanity could have been compelled to participate in such a program. The State was not required to seek a biannual renewal of the obligation to participate in such a program. There was no evidence that the legislature intended for Tenn. Code Ann. § 33-6-621 to apply to insanity acquittees. The court declined to review the patient's challenge to the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 33-7-303 because it was not raised at the trial court level. Finally, the court found that the trial court had the authority to release the patient from his obligation to participate in the program.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Ervin

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 485

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 223413, 223414 and 223415. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.
State v. Ervin, 40 S.W.3d 508, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 267 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), following their convictions by a jury trial, for disrupting a meeting, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-306(a), and, as to one defendant, of resisting arrest, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-602(a). On appeal, they challenged the jury selection, jury instructions, and the sufficiency of the evidence of guilt.


OVERVIEW: The African-American defendants were alleged to have interrupted a city counsel meeting, taking over the podium at a time when they were not scheduled to speak. A videotape of the council meeting was shown to the jury. State v. Quintanilla

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee), convicting him for driving while intoxicated, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a single-vehicle accident. A county deputy saw defendant staggering along the roadside. Defendant admitted that he had been drinking. After failing two sobriety tests, he was arrested. The jury found him guilty of driving with a blood alcohol concentration greater than .10 percent. Code Ann. § 55-10-401. The trial court was not required to suppress statements made by defendant before he was taken into custody. The evidence before the trial court was sufficient to support his conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Price


No. M2002-00991-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


124 S.W.3d 135; 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 403



May 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Ordered published by State v. Price, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1066 (Tenn., Oct. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. Nos. 2002-A-56 and 2001-B-1022. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.
State v. Mahoney, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 937 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 1, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a negotiated plea agreement, defendant pled guilty in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) to 15 counts of money laundering, a Class B felony, and one count of conspiracy to commit money laundering, a Class C felony. Defendant reserved the right to appeal a certified question of law, which challenged the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-14-901, -903 of the Tennessee Money Laundering Act of 1996.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the legislature's exclusion of criminal acts in violation of the gambling statutes from those criminal activities which could lead to punishment for prohibited acts of money laundering violated the equal protection of law provisions of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 and art. I, § 8. The appellate court's review of the legislative history of the Money Laundering Act indicated that the gambling laws were exempted from the definition of "specified unlawful activity" because a majority of the members of the Tennessee House of Representatives did not feel that the money laundering statute should be applied to gambling acts which might be considered minor offenses. The clear implication was that the Tennessee House of Representatives approved the act in order to enable law enforcement to combat money laundering in other offenses considered to be more serious by the legislative body. The legislative history supported the constitutionality of the statute by establishing that the reasonableness of the classification was at least "fairly debatable." Thus, the money laundering statutes did not violate the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

State v. Berry

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, convicted appellant of two counts of first- degree murder, two counts of especially aggravated robbery, and two counts of especially aggravated kidnapping. The trial court imposed two concurrent twenty-five-year sentences for the especially aggravated robbery and the especially aggravated kidnapping convictions. He was sentenced to death for each of the homicides. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a 19-year-old gang member, along with a co-defendant, discussed a robbery of guns and an automobile from the victims. Appellant stated, "If we rob 'em, we gotta kill 'em." PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving while under the influence of an intoxicant, Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401, a Class A misdemeanor. The Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) dismissed defendant's motion for a mistrial. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped after the police officer observed his crossing the dividing lines of a highway. The officer noticed the smell of alcohol as he approached the car. COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 261



March 27, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Jackson, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 330 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 11, 2003)
Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Jackson, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 740 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jackson v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 218 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2000-D-2190. Steve Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) found defendant guilty of aggravated burglary, robbery, misdemeanor theft, attempted rape, aggravated kidnapping, and two counts of rape. The trial court sentenced defendant to an effective term of 34 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the home of the victim, a widow in her 80s, took her by the arm, pushed her down on her bed, covered her head with a pillow, and asked where her money was. Defendant also performed and attempted to perform sexual acts on the victim. The detective informed defendant of his Miranda rights, and defendant effectively waived those rights. Also, the circumstantial evidence was sufficient to establish defendant's identity as the perpetrator. Additionally, because defendant's actions in tying the victim up certainly increased her risk of harm and gave defendant at least some additional time in which to effect his flight, thereby lessening his risk of detection, defendant's aggravated kidnapping conviction was appropriate. Further, the trial court committed reversible error in failing to instruct the jury on sexual battery as a lesser-included offense of aggravated rape and theft as a lesser-included offense of robbery; thus, he had to be retried on the two charges of rape and the robbery charge. Finally, because the trial court properly applied two enhancement factors to defendant's sentences, the length of the terms of each of his sentences were appropriate.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for retrial defendant's convictions of robbery and rape. The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated burglary, attempted rape, aggravated kidnapping, and misdemeanor theft and the effective 22 year sentence for those convictions.

State v. Greenwood


No. M2002-01349-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


115 S.W.3d 527; 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 243


February 12, 2003, Session  
March 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 19, 2003.
Appeal denied by State v. Greenwood, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 830 (Tenn., Sept. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. I-139-901. Donald P. Harris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of driving under the influence of an intoxicant with a blood alcohol content of 0.10 percent or more, third offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the trial court erroneously admitted statements on the videotape of the stop indicating defendant's vehicle would be seized. Defendant argued that this was evidence of other crimes prohibited by Tenn. R. Evid. 404(b). The appellate court was unable to conclude that the jury would have been aware that it was a subsequent DUI. Any error was harmless, as defendant was convicted of DUI per se. Defendant did not show that the state trooper had sufficient expertise to qualify him to give the opinion that defendant's blood alcohol content was rising at the time of the withdrawal of the blood. The trooper's ultimate response was that he did not know whether the blood alcohol content was rising or falling. Expert extrapolation testing was not required in a DUI prosecution. Evidence of defendant's physical condition at the time of arrest or at the time of administration of the test was relevant to the issue of blood alcohol content. The blood withdrawal approximately 55 minutes after the stop was reasonable, and the 0.12 percent result justified the conclusion that defendant had a blood alcohol content of 0.10 percent or more at the time he was driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Waters


No. E2001-00882-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 193


May 21, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
March 6, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application denied by State v. Waters, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 692 (Tenn., July 7, 2003)
Application denied by State v. Waters, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 688 (Tenn., July 21, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Winton v. State, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 686 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 29, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Winton v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 53 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 61974-A. Ray L. Jenkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants were convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County, Tennessee, of especially aggravated kidnapping (Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-305) and attempted aggravated robbery. They were given 25-year sentences as violent offenders, with 100 percent service for aggravated kidnapping, and 6 years as Range I standard offenders for the aggravated robbery convictions, to be served concurrently. They appealed their convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendants attempted to rob four victims at gunpoint, then ordered them into one victim's car. He drove defendants and the others to his home; everyone escaped, though one defendant fired warning shots. Defendants argued that the removal of the victims from the initial scene was incidental to the attempted robbery and, thus, the evidence was insufficient to convict them of aggravated kidnapping. The appellate court disagreed; the attempted aggravated robbery was fully consummated when defendants transported victims at gunpoint to a different location in their hope for further gain. No plea bargain existed to enforce, and the prosecutor was not guilty of misconduct. As defendants made no showing that the pre-trial delay impaired their defense, they failed to establish a speedy trial violation. Neither defendant establish that his trial counsel was ineffective. The trial court improperly applied the enhancement factor of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(3) in finding the offense involved more than one victim, as the jury acquitted defendants of all offenses against all but one of the victims; however, the remaining enhancement factors justified the sentences imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Fritts v. State


No. M2001-03126-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 164


August 14, 2002, Assigned on Briefs

Fritts v. State, 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 685 (Tenn., Sept. 17, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pled guilty to burglary of an automobile and first degree burglary. He subsequently filed in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) a petition for habeas corpus relief. The trial court denied the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged that the plea bargain process employed by the State of Tennessee was unconstitutional per se, thus rendering two of his convictions, which resulted from guilty pleas, void. The appellate court found that the guilty plea process was not unconstitutional, nor was the petitioner deprived of his right to a trial by jury by the trial court's acceptance of his guilty pleas. Accordingly, the appellate court held that he failed to set forth a basis for trial court corpus relief. The appellate court concluded that petitioner was not entitled to relief on any of his convictions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

786 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dowell


No. E2002-01918-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 155


January 22, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
February 24, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Johnson County No. 3953 Lynn W. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Johnson County, Tennessee, convicted defendant for driving while his blood alcohol concentration was .10 percent or greater, a Class A misdemeanor. The trial court sentenced defendant to just under one year with 48 hours to be served in the county jail and the remainder on probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two witnesses testified defendant drove his truck to a shopping center parking lot early one morning. One of the witnesses, the arresting police officer, said that when he spoke with defendant shortly after defendant parked, he smelled the odor of alcohol. Defendant admitted he had consumed two beers that evening, and the officer found a partially consumed can of beer in defendant's truck. A third witness testified he was with defendant during the time period in question and saw defendant drink one or two beers. The trial court found defendant's blood was drawn within 30 to 40 minutes of him driving his truck and that his blood alcohol concentration was .13 percent. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to convict. Specifically, he argued the trial court failed to require the State to prove his blood alcohol content was .10 percent or more at the time he was driving. The appeals court held the evidence was sufficient. The arresting officer's testimony, the police dispatcher's log, and the laboratory report supported the trial court's finding that defendant's blood was drawn within about 40 minutes of his driving. The 40-minute delay was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

787 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vaughn


No. M2001-03091-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 28


September 18, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
January 15, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3, Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2001-C-1405. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of vandalism and aggravated criminal trespass, after waiving a jury trial. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the trial court asked if defendant, who was pro se, wished to proceed with a jury or waive his right to a jury, defendant said he wanted to do whatever would more speedily resolve his case, and he executed a written waiver of his right to a jury trial. The appellate court held defendant was not denied his right to counsel at trial, as counsel was appointed after he waived a jury. While he was entitled to counsel when waiving a jury, and was not advised of that right, the absence of counsel did not invalidate his waiver, as the trial court was responding to his request for a speedy trial, and, if the trial court erred in allowing defendant to waive a jury pro se, counsel did not try to withdraw this waiver, and had adequate time to do so. Defendant did not show he did not understand the waiver or that the absence of counsel prejudiced him. Tenn. R. Crim. P. 23 required only that, in waiving a jury, defendant execute a written waiver, which was done. While the trial court did not have a colloquy with defendant about his waiver, as required absent a written waiver, his waiver, consented to by the prosecutor and the trial court, satisfied the requirements of Rule 23.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

788 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sledge


No. W2001-02402-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 10


July 9, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
January 6, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Sledge, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 520 (Tenn., May 27, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sledge v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1114 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 12, 2005)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Sledge, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 677 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 92-04081. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Sledge, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1184 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 24, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, and especially aggravated robbery in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee). On appeal, the instant court affirmed both convictions, but reversed defendant's death sentence, and remanded it for resentencing. Defendant was then given a life sentence which was ordered to be served consecutively to the original 20-year sentence for especially aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court was required to revisit the issue of whether the new murder sentence was to run consecutive to, or concurrent with, the original robbery sentence when the case was remanded for resentencing. The instant court affirmed the trial court's imposition of consecutive sentencing, remanding to determine the sentence for the first degree murder conviction. While not an explicit limitation of the scope of the remand, the implication of the remand was that the issue of consecutive sentencing need not be revisited. The law of the case doctrine proscribed reconsideration of the issue. None of the limited exceptions to the law of the case doctrine applied to defendant's case. Accordingly, the trial court's refusal to reconsider the issue was not error. Further the trial court correctly applied criteria Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(2) and (4), that defendant was an offender whose record of criminal activity was extensive, and that defendant was a dangerous offender whose behavior indicates little or no regard for human life. None of the evidence defendant presented at the resentencing hearing rebutted the application of those factors.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, ordering the defendant's sentences be served consecutively, was affirmed.

Anderson v. State


No. W2002-00783-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1126



December 31, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Anderson v. Parker, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1096 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C-00-140.
Anderson v. State, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 475 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: MOTION GRANTED. APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Madison County, Tennessee, denied defendant's motion to reopen his post-conviction petition after defendant pled guilty to facilitation to first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit especially aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to reopen his post-conviction petition. The State argued that defendant failed to perfect his application for permission to appeal. The appellate court found that defendant failed to comply with the statutory requirements for seeking appellate review. Defendant filed his application in the wrong court and failed to attach documents filed by the parties in the trial court and in the order of the trial court denying his motion. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-217(c) governed review of a trial court's decision to deny a motion to reopen a post-conviction petition. An appeal as of right was not available for review of a lower court's denial of a motion to reopen a petition for post-conviction relief. The failure of defendant to comply with statutory requirements governing review of a denial of a motion to reopen deprived the appellate court of jurisdiction. Defendant filed his petition for post-conviction relief outside the statute of limitations set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-202(a), and he failed to show that any of his claims was within one of the exceptions set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-202(b).


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Williams v. Myers


No. M2002-00855-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1090


September 18, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
December 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Williams v. Myers, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 429 (Tenn., May 12, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wayne County. No. 12643. Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.
Williams v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 812 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 27, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in 1988 of felony murder and was serving a life sentence. After exhausting his direct and post-conviction appeals, petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which the Circuit Court for Wayne County, Tennessee, subsequently denied. Petitioner appealed the denial of his petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was serving a life sentence for felony murder. Petitioner contended that the trial court lacked the authority to render the judgment against him. A handwritten note by the trial judge on the indictment indicated amendments to the indictment. After some discussion, both of the changes were made during the trial, with the defense's consent. The appellate court concluded that the indictment in this case clearly apprized the petitioner of the crimes of which he was charged, that it furnished the trial court an adequate basis for the entry of its judgment, and that it protected the petitioner from double jeopardy. The indictment, even as modified, was not so defective as to deprive the trial court of jurisdiction. Petitioner also challenged the constitutionality of the 1982 first degree murder statute. The appellate court concluded, however, that the statute in this case was sufficiently precise to have put petitioner on notice of the charges against him. The appellate court also concluded that a person of common intelligence could reasonably understand what acts the statute proscribed. The statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

State v. Rosenbalm


No. E2002-00324-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1045


August 20, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
December 9, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S42,697. Phyllis H. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Sullivan County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of one count of rape and one count of incest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support the rape conviction and that the State impermissibly asked questions about his failure to make a statement to police. The appellate court found that the issue of consent presented a jury question. It was the prerogative of the jury to accredit the victim's testimony. There was sufficient evidence to establish that defendant knew or should have known that his sexual advances upon the victim were not welcome. The record was unclear as to whether defendant had been arrested or advised of his Miranda rights at the time he was interviewed by the detective. Because it was defendant's duty to supply an adequate record for review, the cross-examination about his post-arrest silence was not in error. Any error was harmless as defendant's explanation for his silence--that the detective had failed to advise him of the subject of the interview--was plausible. The trial court properly applied enhancement factors under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114 and two possible mitigating factors warranted little weight. Defendant was ineligible for a community corrections sentence under Tenn. Code ann. § 40-36-106(a)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Orr


No. W2001-02075-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1029



November 27, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Orr, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 471 (Tenn., May 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County. No. 01cr-1636. C. Creed McGinley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Tennessee) of aggravated burglary, aggravated rape, and class E felony theft. He received an effective 25-year sentence. On appeal, defendant raised the following issues for review, inter alia: whether the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress, whether the evidence was sufficient to support the verdicts, and whether his sentence was proper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that evidence found inside his "living quarters" should have been suppressed, as the person who granted the waiver to search was without authority to do so. The evidence established that defendant had been staying at the residence for approximately two to three weeks at the time the search of the premises was conducted. Defendant stated he was staying in his co-defendant's trailer for a time, because he was in between houses. The appellate court concluded, contrary to the ruling of the trial court, that defendant did have a legitimate expectation of privacy in the residence and, therefore, had standing to challenge the validity of the search. The appellate court also concluded that the property owner did not have authority to permit a search of the residence. She did not live at the trailer; therefore, she did not possess authority over its premises. Accordingly, the search of the premises was unconstitutional, and the evidence seized during the search was inadmissible. However, given the strength of the State's case, no prejudice to defendant occurred as a result of the evidence being admitted. Any error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences of the circuit court were affirmed.

Hereford v. State


No. E2002-01222-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 968


August 20, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
November 13, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 239059. Douglas A. Meyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief by the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee). Petitioner alleged: his convictions were void; misrepresentation by his trial counsel; and that he was entitled to DNA analysis of physical evidence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner challenged his 1994 convictions for aggravated burglary and theft. Petitioner alleged that his trial counsel told him he would receive an effective sentence of 42 years, and he instead received a sentence of 52 years. Petitioner also alleged that his trial counsel told him he would be released when he served 60 percent of his sentence, while the Department of Corrections advised him that he would only be eligible for release upon serving 60 percent of his sentence. Petitioner also claimed he was serving sentences that were not based on any convictions. Finally, petitioner claimed he should have been entitled to the State's trial exhibits so that he could conduct DNA tests on the exhibits. The appellate court held that petitioner's claim that he was serving an illegal sentence was barred by the statute of limitations. Petitioner's claim that counsel misrepresented his effective sentence was also denied, as it was also barred by the statute of limitations. Finally, the trial court did not err in not allowing defendant to examine the State's trial exhibits to have them tested for DNA, as petitioner failed to give the court a basis to order such tests.


OUTCOME: The denial by the trial court of the petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

State v. Owens


No. W2001-01397-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 974


June 5, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
November 8, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed as Modified. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Haywood County. No. 4436A & B. Terry Lafferty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, husband and wife, were convicted of child abuse. Both defendants challenged the sufficiency of the convicting evidence and the failure of the Circuit Court for Haywood County (Tennessee) to grant a judgment of acquittal. The wife's sentences were to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of abusing their foster children by whipping them and burning them with cigarettes. Defendants argued that the evidence was insufficient and that the trial judge should have granted their motion for acquittals. The appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient, as the jury chose to believe the testimony of a doctor and one of the victims as to the nature of the abuse over that of defendants', who denied abusing the children or having knowledge of the cord that was used to whip the children. The appellate court held the trial court did not err in allowing the wife to be questioned about the income she received from the State for being a foster parent, as it went to the wife's claims of altruistic motives for taking the children. Also, questions regarding the husband's prior record of abuse of children was not in error, as the objection to the admission of the evidence was not preserved, and there was insufficient evidence to find plain error. It was not error not to give a "missing witness" instruction, as the wife failed to establish the availability of the children. The imposition of consecutive sentences on the wife was reversed.


OUTCOME: The convictions of both defendants were affirmed, but the wife's sentence was modified such that the sentences were to be served concurrently.

September 25, 2002, Assigned on Briefs

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Swiggett v. State, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 78 (Tenn., Feb. 3, 2003)
Discretionary appeal not allowed by Swiggett v. State, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 106 (Tenn., Feb. 3, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Swiggett v. Carlton, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 123 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Greene County. No. 02CR001. James E. Beckner, Judge.
State v. Swiggett, 1994 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 766 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 23, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Greene County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of first degree premeditated murder and denied his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted as grounds for post-conviction relief that he had newly discovered evidence; that his indictment was unconstitutional; and that his jury instructions were unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the trial court erred by dismissing the petition on the basis of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-202(c), as defendant's prior petition was not resolved on the merits but was dismissed as time-barred. However, the petition was subject to summary dismissal on the grounds that it was time barred under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-202(a). Defendant's complaint was that his indictment and jury instructions did not sufficiently differentiate the terms "premeditation" and "deliberation." Prior caselaw did not create a new constitutional right requiring the appellate court to reexamine defendant's indictment and jury instructions. Defendant's assertion did not rise to the level of new evidence required to toll the statute of limitations, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-202(b)(2). Defendant's claim for relief upon error coram nobis was also time-barred, because it was not filed within one year of the date on which the judgment of conviction became final in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

The state supreme court affirmed the conviction but remanded for a resentencing hearing, which again resulted in defendant's sentence to death. He appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Smith County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of first-degree murder, and defendant appealed from his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murdering his former wife. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the convicting evidence, as it related to the element of premeditation; and the trial court's ruling which he asserted interfered with the defense's order of proof, thus, forcing a premature election on defendant's right to testify. The court of criminal appeals held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The court of criminal appeals also held that the trial court did not reversibly err by insisting defendant testify before his other witnesses testified.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Blount County. Nos. C-11329, C-11330. D. Kelly Thomas, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Blount County, Tennessee, convicted defendant of two counts of first degree premeditated murder and imposed concurrent sentences of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The jury also convicted defendant of aggravated robbery, and the trial court sentenced the defendant to 25 years' incarceration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised the following issues: (1) whether the trial court properly instructed the jury on all lesser-included offenses raised by the evidence, (2) whether the trial court erred by refusing to instruct the jury on duress, necessity and accessory after the fact, (3) whether the trial court erred by allowing into evidence testimony regarding the defendant's pending aggravated assault trial, (4) whether the trial court erred by allowing into evidence a magazine clip confiscated from the defendant by police two months before the murders, (5) whether the trial court erred by refusing to find the sentencing provisions of the Tennessee homicide laws to be unconstitutional, (6) whether the defendant's convictions for aggravated robbery and theft violated his right against double jeopardy, (7) whether the indictment was constitutionally defective on its face, and (8) whether there was sufficient evidence. Rejecting defendant's contentions, the appellate court found no reversible error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed. The matter was remanded for entry of a corrected judgment form.

State v. Sanders


No. M2000-03083-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 756



August 30, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Dismissed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Coffee County. No. 27,386F. L. Craig Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed in part; reversed and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Coffee County Circuit Court (Tennessee) of aggravated rape, especially aggravated kidnapping, and three alternate counts of first degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the movement and confinement of the victim was essentially incidental to the accomplishment of the aggravated rape and first degree murder and was, therefore, insufficient to support a separate conviction for especially aggravated kidnapping. The court of appeals agreed. The evidence established that the victim's pants and panties were pulled down around her ankles, which restricted the use of her legs. Additionally, her shirt was raised, and her arms tucked inside, which restricted the use of her arms. Finally, she was gagged with her own socks. The restraint of the victim was incidental to the rape and did not support a separate conviction for kidnapping. Notwithstanding the resulting restraint of the victim's movement, removal of the victim's clothing was part and parcel of the act of rape. Because there was no other evidence of any further confinement, movement, or restraint of the victim, defendant's conviction for especially aggravated kidnapping was not supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for especially aggravated kidnapping was reversed and dismissed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.
